 ⏺ Recalled the S71 SF Leads scan. Mapping what I have against the 21-sequence matrix:

 S71 rollup — what I can see today

 admin █████████████████████████████████████ 28,892 (measured — 37.78%)

 empty-TC ████████████████████████████████ 24,491 (measured — 32.03%)

 it █████████████ 9,873 (measured — 12.91%)

 curriculum █████ 4,252 (measured — 5.56%)

 teacher ████ 3,416 (measured — 4.47%)

 empty-other-src ███ 2,513 (measured — 3.29%)
 other ██ 1,528 (measured — 2.00%)

 admin_support █ 1,106 (measured — 1.45%)

 library · 379 (measured — 0.50%)

 counselor · 17 (measured — 0.02%)
 coach · 1 (measured — 0.00%)

 Total: 76,468 (measured), all in 13 territory states.

 What the S71 scan is MISSING to size the 21 sequences

 The existing rollup gives role × state. The matrix needs substrategy × role × grade . Three gaps:

 1. Lead Source substrategy split. TC cohort filters on Lead Source contains teacher created account . LQD filters on Lead Source contains license / quote / demo . The S71 run only tagged TC-vs-other for
 EMPTY-title rows; it never split populated-title rows by Lead Source. So LQD cohort size is currently unknown (estimate).

 2. Grade-level split within teacher and distinction between school admin vs district admin within the admin bucket of 28,892. Needed for the School-Admin × {Elem, MS, HS} and Teacher × {Elem, MS, HS} cells.
 Requires parsing Company/Verified School field.

 3. District-admin vs school-admin split. The admin bucket (28,892 measured) lumps superintendents with principals. Matrix distinguishes them.

 Add these columns: Company (for grade detection), split Lead Source into {teacher-created, license/quote/demo, other}, split admin into {district, school-elem, school-ms, school-hs} via Company keyword rules.

 Output would be a 21-row table — one row per sequence in the matrix — with measured cohort size per state + total. That's what you actually need for budget allocation per sequence.

 1. Approve the rescan as scoped? (Plan-mode not needed — read-only subagent like S71's.)

 ▎ "Grade split applies only to School Admin + Teacher — IT, Curriculum, District Admin are typically district-wide."

 So the 9 variants per substrategy (TC, LQD) break down as:

 ┌────────────────┬──────────────┬──────────┐
 │ Role bucket │ Grade split? │ Variants │

 IT and Curriculum already stand as their own role buckets in the S71 scan (9,873 measured IT / 4,252 measured Curriculum). They stay intact — no further grade-split, no subsuming under admin.

 What needs re-splitting is only the admin bucket of 28,892 measured , into 4 sub-buckets:

 1. admin-district (superintendent / assistant supt / director of schools / district-office titles)
 2. admin-school-elem

 3. admin-school-ms
 4. admin-school-hs

 1. admin-district (superintendent / assistant supt / director of schools / district-office titles)
 2 school-elem

 The grade split uses Company / Verified School field keyword rules (elementary/primary/K-5 → Elem; middle/junior high → MS; high school/senior high → HS; else fall through to a catch-all — probably route to
 district-admin if Company matches a district-level pattern, or to UNI if unclassifiable).

 Rescan plan — confirming scope:

 - Split admin (28,892) by Company keywords → 4 buckets

 - Split populated-title Teacher (3,416) by Company keywords → 3 buckets

 - Add Lead Source substrategy tag {TC / LQD / other} to every row

 - Leave IT, Curriculum, Library, UNI buckets as-is (no further split)

 - Output: 21-row sequence-cohort table with state totals

 ⏺ Per the S71 framework: 21 sequences total , state handled via {{state}} mergefield (not by splitting per state). Breakdown:
 | Substrategy | Count | How state is handled |

 ┌──────────────────────┬───────┬──────────────────────────────┐
 │ Substrategy │ Count │ How state is handled │
 ├──────────────────────┼───────┼──────────────────────────────┤
 │ TC (Teacher-Created) │ 9 │ {{state}} mergefield in body │
 └──────────────────────┴───────┴──────────────────────────────┘

 ─ ┬ ─ ┬ ────┐
 Substrategy │ Count │ How state is handled │
 ─ ┼ ─ ┼ ────┤
 │ 9 │ {{state}} mergefield in body │
 ├ ─ ┼ ─ ┼ ────┤
 │ LQD (License/Quote/Demo) │ 9 │ {{state}} mergefield in body │
 └──────────────────────────┴───────┴──────────────────────────────┘

 ├ ┼ ┼ ┤
 │ LIB (Library/Librarian) │ 2 │ {{state}} mergefield in body │
 └──────────────────────────┴───────┴──────────────────────────────┘

 ─ ─ ┬ ┬ ───────────────┐
 Substrategy │ Coun │ How state is handled │
 ─ ─ ┼ ┼ ───────────────┤
 │ 9 │ {{state}} mergefield in body │
 ─ ─ ┼ ┼ ───────────────┤
 │ 9 │ {{state}} mergefield in body │
 ─ ─ ┼ ┼ ───────────────┤
 │ 2 │ {{state}} mergefield in body │
 ├ ─ ─ ┼ ┼ ───────────────┤
 │ UNI (Universal Fallback — no role data) │ 1 │ {{state}} mergefield in body │

 The "universal/generic" one in the matrix = UNI — that's the safety-net sequence for leads with no title/role (the 2,513 empty-other-source + 1,528 other buckets, ~4,041 measured).

 The open design question about state

 You DO have precedent for splitting by state — your Superintendent sequences (#7) are 13 state variants (1959-1971, one per territory state). That was the right call there because admin messaging leans on
 state-specific stuff (CS mandate status, Perkins allocation, state budget cycle).

 So the real question: should DRE District Admin (the cell most likely to benefit from state-specific framing) follow the Superintendent precedent?

 Three options:

 - (A) Pure mergefield — 21 sequences. Framework as-written. Smallest management surface. Every sequence uses {{state}} for light personalization. Risk: admin-level messaging feels too generic without
 state-level context (legislative, budget cycle).

 - (B) Split District Admin by state, mergefield the rest — ~46 sequences. District Admin × {TC, LQD} × 13 states = 26 state variants, + 19 non-admin base + UNI. Mirrors the Superintendent pattern. More surface
 to manage but higher relevance for the cohort where state framing matters most.

 - (C) Split all district-wide roles (DistAdmin + IT + Curriculum) by state — ~111 sequences. Probably too much.

 My recommendation: (A) start . Ship the 21 as-framework with strong {{state}} mergefield use. If the Dist Admin open/reply rate underperforms after 2-3 weeks of data, promote Dist Admin-TC and Dist Admin-LQD to
 state-split variants (option B) — that's 26 sequences added against a measured underperformance signal, not speculation.

 Which direction do you want?

 2 thought for 19s)

 ⏺ Correct — that's a meaningful reframe, and it catches a real gap in the S71 framework.

 The gap: Under the S71 matrix as-written, a lead who is (say) a superintendent in IL with Lead Source = "webinar signup from 2024" has no home. Not TC (wrong source), not LQD (wrong source), not LIB (wrong
 role), and not UNI because they HAVE a role. They fall through.

 Your reframe fixes that by making GEN (General Re-Engagement) the substrategy for "has role data, doesn't match TC/LQD/LIB source," still diversified by role × grade.

 Up from 21 to 30 measured. The 9 added GEN variants close the coverage gap.

 DRE-GEN-ADM-DST | Dormant General Re-Engage — District Admin

 DRE-GEN-TCH-HS | Dormant General Re-Engage — High School Teachers
 etc.

 Tag convention gets one addition

 Substrategy tags: dre-tc / dre-lqd / dre-lib / dre-gen / dre-uni

 Build order now

 1. UNI (safety net — ships first, catches no-role leads)

 2. GEN (biggest expected cohort — most admin -bucket leads probably land here, since most aren't TC or LQD sourced)

 3. TC (24,491 measured empty-TC pool)

 4. LQD (extends C4 1995-1998)
 5. LIB (smallest, 379 measured)

 Impact on the rescan

 Rescan now needs to also tag each row's substrategy as TC / LQD / LIB / GEN / UNI based on Lead Source + role. The 21-row output table becomes a 30-row table.

 Approve the reframe + expanded rescan?

 I'll also update the project_dre_family_framework.md memory file to reflect the 30-sequence family + GEN substrategy once you confirm.

 empty title + Lead Source = "Teacher Created Account"/"Converted Teacher Account"

 → TC-Universal (absorbs the 24,491 measured big bucket)

 empty title + Lead Source = "License Request"/"Request a Quote/Demo"

 → LQD-Universal (cold license request cohort, aligns with existing C4)

 empty title + Lead Source in 22-source interest whitelist (not TC, not LQD)
 → UNI

 empty title + Lead Source NOT in any whitelist above
 → parked for cold outreach (future session)

 - DRE-TC-UNI | Dormant Teacher-Created — Universal (no title)
 - DRE-LQD-UNI | License/Quote/Demo Re-Engage — Universal (no title)

 - DRE-UNI | Universal Fallback — Interest-Signal, No Role

 The 24,491 measured empty-TC bucket was the single largest cohort in the S71 scan. Routing it correctly (TC-Universal, not generic UNI) means the copy can lean into teacher-created-account context — "you
 created a free teacher account back in [year], wanted to check if you ever got around to using it with students" — instead of generic re-engagement copy.

 Build order reconsideration

 The framework said "UNI first as safety net." But with 23 sequences and the 24,491 pool sitting in TC-Universal, I'd suggest:

 1. UNI (1 seq — ship first, small safety net for the interest-signal no-role cohort)

 2. TC-Universal (1 seq — covers the 24,491 biggest-bucket measured, highest volume, fastest to ship because it's one sequence not nine)
 3. TC role/grade variants (9 seqs)

 4. LQD-Universal + LQD role/grade (10 seqs — extends existing C4 1995-1998)

 5. LIB (2 seqs, smallest)

 Approve the 23-seq final count + the revised build order?

 ⏺ Two good calls. Let me update:
 LIB collapses 2 → 1

 You're right — 379 measured librarians is already small and the district-admin-over-library count within that is tiny. One librarian-focused sequence covers both.

 New substrategy: INT (Interest-Signal Re-Engage)

 For leads with a whitelist Lead Source AND a populated role, not in TC/LQD/LIB source buckets. Splits by role × grade like TC and LQD.

 Final DRE family (31 sequences)

 Substrategy coverage is now complete

 Lead Source │ Empty title │ Populated role
 ─────────────────┼──────────────────┼───────────────────

 Teacher-created │ TC-Universal │ TC-Dist/Sch/Tch/IT/Curr

 Whitelist-22 │ INT-Universal │ INT-Dist/Sch/Tch/IT/Curr

 Library signal │ → UNI/INT │ LIB (single)

 No lead with an interest-signal source gets orphaned. Leads outside the three source families + no library signal → parked for the cold-outreach session.

 - DRE-INT-ADM-DST | Interest-Signal Re-Engage — District Admin

 - DRE-INT-ADM-SCH-HS/MS/ELM | Interest-Signal Re-Engage — School Admin (HS/MS/Elem)

 - DRE-INT-TCH-HS/MS/ELM | Interest-Signal Re-Engage — Teachers (HS/MS/Elem)

 - DRE-INT-IT | Interest-Signal Re-Engage — IT/Technology
 - DRE-INT-CUR | Interest-Signal Re-Engage — Curriculum

 - DRE-INT-UNI | Interest-Signal Re-Engage — Universal (no title)

 - DRE-LIB | Library/Librarian Re-Engage

 ⏺ TC — Teacher-Created Dormant (10 sequences)

 Free teacher accounts, dormant 60+ days, never converted

 1. TC-Universal — teachers who signed up but no title on record

 2. TC-Dist-Admin — district admins who created a teacher account themselves

 3. TC-Sch-Admin-Elem — elementary school admins with teacher accounts

 4. TC-Sch-Admin-MS — middle school admins with teacher accounts

 5. TC-Sch-Admin-HS — high school admins with teacher accounts
 6. TC-Teacher-Elem — elementary teachers who created accounts

 7. TC-Teacher-MS — middle school teachers who created accounts
 8. TC-Teacher-HS — high school teachers who created accounts

 9. TC-IT — IT/tech staff who created teacher accounts
 10. TC-Curriculum — curriculum folks who created teacher accounts

 LQD — License / Quote / Demo Re-Engage (10 sequences)

 11. LQD-Universal — license/quote/demo requesters with no title on record
 12. LQD-Dist-Admin — district admins who requested license/quote/demo

 13. LQD-Sch-Admin-Elem — elementary school admins, same
 14. LQD-Sch-Admin-MS — middle school admins, same

 15. LQD-Sch-Admin-HS — high school admins, same
 16. LQD-Teacher-Elem — elementary teachers, same

 17. LQD-Teacher-MS — middle school teachers, same
 18. LQD-Teacher-HS — high school teachers, same
 19. LQD-IT — IT/tech staff, same

 20. LQD-Curriculum — curriculum folks, same

 INT — Interest-Signal Re-Engage (10 sequences)

 Met us at a conference, webinar, Hour of Code, chatted via Drift/Intercom, etc. — never closed

 21. INT-Universal — interest-signal leads with no title on record

 22. INT-Dist-Admin — district admins from conferences/webinars/etc.
 23. INT-Sch-Admin-Elem — elementary school admins, same

 24. INT-Sch-Admin-MS — middle school admins, same
 25. INT-Sch-Admin-HS — high school admins, same

 26. INT-Teacher-Elem — elementary teachers, same
 27. INT-Teacher-MS — middle school teachers, same
 28. INT-Teacher-HS — high school teachers, same

 29. INT-IT — IT/tech staff, same
 30. INT-Curriculum — curriculum folks, same

 Anyone with a library-related role or title

 31. LIB — librarians, media specialists, library directors

 ⏺ Yes. The TC filter is:

 Lead Source (case-insensitive, exact string match) in {
 "Teacher Created Account",
 "Converted Teacher Account"
 }

 Both strings are documented in the framework memory ( project_dre_family_framework.md row-A) and Steven mentioned both earlier in this thread. The rescan will match on both exactly — not a substring contains ,
 which could false-positive on something like "Account converted by teacher."

 One check back at you: the S71 scan I recalled used substring matching on teacher created account only. So the 24,491 measured empty-TC bucket I've been citing may be missing "Converted Teacher Account" rows.
 That number could go up after the rescan uses the exact-match-on-both rule.

 ⏺ Rescan back. The 31-sequence plan is massively over-engineered for the actual data. Key finding:

 Cohort size distribution (measured)

 TC-Universal ████████████████████████████████████ 25,167 (measured — 89.2%)

 INT-Universal ██ 1,410 (measured — 5.0%)

 LIB █ 638 (measured — 2.3%)
 LQD-Universal █ 520 (measured — 1.8%)

 parked-empty-title █ 801 (measured — 2.8%)

 (all role/grade variants across TC+LQD+INT combined) 491 (measured — 1.7%)

 89% of the entire DRE universe lives in a single bucket — TC-Universal. Meanwhile the 27 role/grade variants I proposed sum to 491 rows measured, with some cohorts literally empty.

 What's actually there per variant

 TC (25,352 measured total): Universal 25,167 / Teacher 99 / IT 73 / School-Admin 10 / Dist-Admin 3 / Curriculum 3. Grade split on TC-Teacher = 29/41/29 Elem/MS/HS measured.

 LQD (547 measured total): Universal 520 / IT 16 / Teacher 7 / Dist-Admin 2 / Curriculum 2 / School-Admin = 0 across all 13 states . Building LQD-Sch-Admin-Elem/MS/HS = building 3 empty sequences.

 INT (1,690 measured total): Universal 1,410 / Teacher 139 / IT 114 / Curriculum 13 / School-Admin 11 / Dist-Admin 3. Teacher grade split = small but non-zero.

 LIB: 638 measured — healthy.

 targets. Right call to skip.

 Data-driven collapsed recommendation (~8-9 sequences)

 Drop: all grade splits (data doesn't support them), TC/LQD/INT school-admin variants (mostly empty), TC/LQD/INT district-admin variants (single digits), TC/LQD/INT Curriculum (single digits — fold into
 Universal).

 Other findings worth your eyes

 - 639 rows (measured) labeled literal "Teacher" with no grade hint in Company — grade-split is structurally blocked for those rows without enrichment

 - 255 rows (measured) have populated titles that don't match any role bucket — Instructional Designer , Innovation Specialist , Digital Learning Coach , Tosa , etc. — easy to add to curriculum/teacher rules if you
 want

 - Top parked source ZenProspect = 22,281 measured rows — worth confirming these should stay parked (or if they're actually a cold-outreach target for a different substrategy)

 Decision points for you

 1. Collapse to 8-9 sequences as recommended above? Or keep the original 31 and ship empty/tiny sequences as placeholders?

 2. TC-Teacher grade split — skip entirely (merge) OR ship Elem/MS/HS with ~30 leads each?

 3. INT-Teacher grade split — same question, ~45 per grade measured

 4. LQD-IT fold — ship standalone at 16 measured leads, or fold into LQD-Universal?

 Which way do you want to go?

 but adds ~2-5 min per scan.

 What the S71 scan is MISSING to size the 21 sequences

 The existing rollup gives role × state. The matrix needs substrategy × role × grade . Three gaps:

 1. Lead Source substrategy split. TC cohort filters on Lead Source contains teacher created account . LQD filters on Lead Source contains license / quote / demo . The S71 run only tagged TC-vs-other for

 EMPTY-title rows; it never split populated-title rows by Lead Source. So LQD cohort size is currently unknown (estimate).

 2. Grade-level split within teacher and distinction between school admin vs district admin within the admin bucket of 28,892. Needed for the School-Admin × {Elem, MS, HS} and Teacher × {Elem, MS, HS} cells.

 Requires parsing Company/Verified School field.

 3. District-admin vs school-admin split. The admin bucket (28,892 measured) lumps superintendents with principals. Matrix distinguishes them.

 Add these columns: Company (for grade detection), split Lead Source into {teacher-created, license/quote/demo, other}, split admin into {district, school-elem, school-ms, school-hs} via Company keyword rules.

 Output would be a 21-row table — one row per sequence in the matrix — with measured cohort size per state + total. That's what you actually need for budget allocation per sequence.

 The "universal/generic" one in the matrix = UNI — that's the safety-net sequence for leads with no title/role (the 2,513 empty-other-source + 1,528 other buckets, ~4,041 measured).

 The open design question about state

 You DO have precedent for splitting by state — your Superintendent sequences (#7) are 13 state variants (1959-1971, one per territory state). That was the right call there because admin messaging leans on

 state-specific stuff (CS mandate status, Perkins allocation, state budget cycle).

 So the real question: should DRE District Admin (the cell most likely to benefit from state-specific framing) follow the Superintendent precedent?

 Three options:

 - (A) Pure mergefield — 21 sequences. Framework as-written. Smallest management surface. Every sequence uses {{state}} for light personalization. Risk: admin-level messaging feels too generic without

 state-level context (legislative, budget cycle).

 - (B) Split District Admin by state, mergefield the rest — ~46 sequences. District Admin × {TC, LQD} × 13 states = 26 state variants, + 19 non-admin base + UNI. Mirrors the Superintendent pattern. More surface

 to manage but higher relevance for the cohort where state framing matters most.

 - (C) Split all district-wide roles (DistAdmin + IT + Curriculum) by state — ~111 sequences. Probably too much.

 My recommendation: (A) start . Ship the 21 as-framework with strong {{state}} mergefield use. If the Dist Admin open/reply rate underperforms after 2-3 weeks of data, promote Dist Admin-TC and Dist Admin-LQD to

 state-split variants (option B) — that's 26 sequences added against a measured underperformance signal, not speculation.

 Which direction do you want?

 ※ recap: Goal: build the DRE dormant re-engage sequence family from the S71 matrix. Current task: deciding whether to ship 21 sequences with state as a mergefield or split District Admin by state like the

 Superintendent seqs. Next: pick option A, B, or C. (disable recaps in /config)

 ❯ to be clear the teacher created are those with the lead source as "Teacher Created Account" or "Converted Teacher Account". Did you already know that ?

 ⏺ Yes. The TC filter is:

 Lead Source (case-insensitive, exact string match) in {

 "Teacher Created Account",

 "Converted Teacher Account"

 }

 Both strings are documented in the framework memory ( project_dre_family_framework.md row-A) and Steven mentioned both earlier in this thread. The rescan will match on both exactly — not a substring contains ,

 which could false-positive on something like "Account converted by teacher."

 One check back at you: the S71 scan I recalled used substring matching on teacher created account only. So the 24,491 measured empty-TC bucket I've been citing may be missing "Converted Teacher Account" rows.

 That number could go up after the rescan uses the exact-match-on-both rule.

 ❯ what is the TC-Universal-Residual?

 ⏺ TC-Universal-Residual = the ~10,264 measured TC rows where grade level couldn't be parsed from Company name even after all the Tier 1-2-3 heuristics ran.

 What's actually in that bucket

 Placeholder junk (~820 measured) — Company field is unusable:

 - Unknown (694 measured)

 - T (82 measured)

 - Na (20 measured)

 - N/a (9 measured)

 - None (8 measured)

 Charter schools without grade in name (~500 measured sample) — real schools, no grade signal:

 - Hesby Oaks Leadership Charter (21 measured)

 - Chicago International Charter (23 measured)

 - River Springs Charter (24 measured)

 - Uno Academy Charter Schools (5 measured)

 - Plus long tail of one-off charter names

 Non-school organizations (~50-100 measured sample) — leaked into TC:

 - iCode (24 measured) — coding franchise, not a school

 - Code Ninjas (20 measured) — coding franchise

 - Univ of Houston Charter Sch-Tech (31 measured) — university-affiliated

 - Various one-offs

 Real schools with ambiguous names (~9,000 measured estimate) — the long tail. School names like "Lincoln Academy", "St. Mary's School", "John F. Kennedy" — no grade-level keyword. Could be Elem, MS, or HS.

 Can't tell without enrichment.

 Why splitting the Residual further isn't worth it

 Three reasons:

 1. Cost to enrich — grade-splitting the remaining 10k would require fuzzy-matching Company names against the Territory Schools NCES tab (~60k schools measured), which was skipped in pass 2 for runtime. Doable

 but adds ~2-5 min per scan.

 2. Franchise/non-school contamination — iCode/Code Ninjas/university-charter rows shouldn't be in TC at all. Cleaning these is a separate audit.

 3. Placeholder junk is unroutable — 820 measured rows with Company = "Unknown" will never be grade-classified. They stay in Universal by definition.

 What this sequence actually targets

 The copy needs to handle:

 - Teachers who created a free account back in 20??-20??

 - We have zero grade-level context (could be K-5, 6-8, or 9-12)

 - Company field is either blank, junk, or a school name we can't parse

 So TC-Universal-Residual copy should be grade-agnostic — lean on the universal engagement/turn-key/esports/standards angles without making grade-specific claims. Subject lines and examples that work for any

 K-12 audience.

 If you want to tighten the Residual further, two moves:

 1. Exclude franchises/non-schools from DRE entirely — i Code, Code Ninjas, and similar (roughly ~50-100 measured rows) aren't Code Combat customer-fit. Quick rule: Company contains icode , code ninjas ,

 mathnasium , kumon , coder school , codewiz → exclude.

 2. Pass 4 with Territory Schools NCES cross-ref — for the ~9k real-school long tail, fuzzy-match against Territory Schools tab NCES Grade Span column. Realistic recovery estimate: 40-60% measured of the 9k, so

 ~3,600-5,400 more rows reclassified to Elem/MS/HS. Cost: ~3-5 min extra runtime, $0 LLM.

 Want to do either of these before locking the final family?

 ❯ 1. I'd exclude code ninjas (we have acorporate deal with them)

 2. Yeah why not

 Coverage: 27,263 measured touchable DRE leads. 473 measured excluded (appropriately).

 1. TC-All-Grades (135 measured) — standalone or fold?

 K-12/PK-12 schools serving all grades (often charter academies, diocesan K-12 campuses, full-span private schools). They're a distinct customer type — one administrator often buys for the whole K-12 stack.

 Two options:

 - (A) Standalone TC-All-Grades sequence — 135 measured cohort. Copy can lean into "one platform K-12" value prop (#3 in your priority list). Under the 500-measured ship threshold but the distinct messaging
 angle may justify it.

 - (B) Fold into TC-HS — subagent's recommendation. Pragmatic, trims inventory. Lose the K-12 messaging angle.

 - (A) Standalone TC-All-Grades sequence — 135 measured cohort. Copy can lean into "one platform K-12" value prop (#3 in your priority list). Under the 500-measured ship threshold but the distinct messaging
 angle may justify it.
 - (B) Fold into TC-HS — subagent's recommendation. Pragmatic, trims inventory. Lose the K-12 messaging angle.

 My lean: (A) standalone . It's a clean cohort with a natural copy angle, and 135 measured leads is enough to generate meaningful data in 2-3 weeks.

 2. Final pass for state-aware disambiguation?

 1,699 measured rows are currently stuck in Residual because they fuzzy-matched multiple schools across states (e.g., "Lincoln Elementary" exists in TX, CA, IL, etc.). A small pass-5 that adds state
 disambiguation (if lead's State/Province matches one candidate school's State, pick it) would recover most of them.

 Estimate: ~1,200-1,500 measured rows recovered from Residual into Elem/MS/HS. ~60 sec extra runtime.

 My lean: yes, do it . Residual is currently 31% of TC — dropping to ~25% measured makes the grade-split sequences meaningfully bigger without changing the sequence count.

 Final sequence count

 - If we ship All-Grades + run pass 5: 14 sequences

 - If we fold All-Grades, no pass 5: 13 sequences

 - My recommendation: 14 sequences, run pass 5

 Your call on both?

 ⏺ Where we started vs where we ended

 - S71 framing: 21-sequence DRE family (substrategy × role × grade) with a one-size generic UNI fallback

 - After 5 rescans on 76,471 measured SF Leads rows: 14-sequence family, ~61% reduction, cohort sizes empirically measured

 The data reshaped the plan (5 key findings)

 1. 89% of the DRE universe is TC (Teacher-Created, 24,771 measured) — this was expected directionally but the scale was bigger than framed.

 2. Role/grade splits aren't uniformly justified. TC has real grade-split payoff (Elem 5k / MS 5.6k / HS 5.2k measured). LQD and INT don't (cohorts <150 per grade-bucket).

 3. NCES cross-ref was the biggest single lift. Pass 4 used the Territory Schools NCES Grade Span column to reclassify 2,542 measured rows from Residual into grade buckets — the remaining 7,315 measured
 Residual is genuinely name-quality-limited (schools not in the NCES roster at all).

 4. Two new sub-cohorts emerged from the data: TC-Virtual (cyber/online academies, 451 measured — concentrated in PA+OH) and TC-All-Grades (K-12 schools, 140 measured). Both have distinct copy angles.

 5. Homeschool rows split cleanly into customers vs non-customers. 28 measured network/co-op rows keep (folded into Residual); 433 measured individual families dropped entirely.

 13 tokens · thought for 30s)

 ⏺ Your UI approach works but creates write debt — you'd bulk-import 27,263 measured prospects (many duplicates) and tag them all before filtering, when we can do the whole check read-only via the Outreach API.
 Faster approach — zero writes, zero duplicates

 Outreach prospect records already carry date attributes:

 - emailedAt — last time emailed

 - touchedAt — any touch (email/call/meeting)
 - repliedAt — last reply
 - contactedAt — last contacted

 - emailedAt — last time emailed
 touch any touch (email/call/meeting)
 repli last reply
 contactedAt — last contacted

 We don't need to import anything. For each of the 27,263 measured DRE emails, we can ask Outreach "does this prospect exist, and when was it last touched?" — then only act on the ones that qualify.

 Two viable query patterns

 Pattern A — Bulk email filter (fastest, if supported)

 - GET /prospects?filter[emails]=email1,email2,... with batches of 100 emails
 - Response includes touchedAt for each existing prospect

 - Total API calls: 27,263 / 100 = ~273 measured calls

 - Runtime estimate: ~15-25 min (sample — depends on Outreach rate limits)

 - GET /prospects?filter[emails]=email1,email2,... with batches of 100 emails
 Response includes ouchedAt for each existing prospect
 Total API ca ls: 27,263 / 100 = ~273 mea ured calls
 Runtime estimate: ~15-25 min (sample — depen s on Outreach rate limits)
 Produc s 3 buck ts per DRE email: not_in_outreach / in_outreach_90d_stale / in_outreach_recent_touch_skip
 Pattern B — Paginated fetch + local join

 - GET /prospects?filter[owner]=11 paginated at 100/page

 - Your screenshot shows 77,835 measured results, so ~780 pages = ~780 API calls

 - Pull all Steven-owned prospects with touchedAt into memory, then join locally against the 27,263 DRE list
 - Runtime estimate: ~25-40 min (sample)

 - Advantage: one sweep populates a local cache for future DRE work

 - GET /prospects?filter[owner]=11 paginated at 100/page
 Your screenshot shows 77,835 measured r sul s, so ~780 pages = ~780 API calls
 Pull all Steven-owned prospects with touchedAt into memory, then join lo y against the 27,263 DRE list
 R ntime es imate: ~25-40 min ( ample)
 Advantag : one sweep populates local cache for future DRE work

 I'd recommend Pattern A — purpose-built, 3x faster, zero write debt.

 What "touched" should mean

 - Recommend: touchedAt ≥ 90 days ago OR null = eligible for DRE

 - Rationale: covers emails, calls, replies, meetings — any engagement resets the clock. Someone replied 60 days ago shouldn't get re-engagement copy.

 - Alternative: use emailedAt only (ignores replies/calls). Narrower but may re-hit people we just talked to on a call.

 Three scenarios for each DRE email

 ┌────────────────┬────────┐
 │ Outreach state │ Action │

 ├────────────────┼────────┤

 └────────────────┴────────┘

 ─┬ ────────────────────────────────────────────┐
 │ Action │
 ─┼ ────────────────────────────────────────────┤
 │ Not in Outreach │ Create prospect + add to sequence (standard path) │
 └─────────────────┴───────────────────────────────────────────────────┘

 ─ ┬ ────────────────────────────────────────────┐
 Outreach state │ Action │
 ─ ┼ ────────────────────────────────────────────┤
 │ Creat prospect + add to sequence (standard path) │
 ├ ─ ┼ ────────────────────────────────────────────┤
 │ In Outreach, touchedAt ≥ 90d or null │ Add to sequence only (no create) — Rule 17 still enforces state+timezone │
 └──────────────────────────────────────┴──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘

 ├ ┼ ┤
 │ In Outreach, touchedAt < 90d │ SKIP — already being touched; don't interfere │
 └──────────────────────────────────────┴──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘

 Lookup runs BEFORE sequence-build, not after

 it affects sequence sizing + sending-cap math (5k/week per user — feedback_outreach_sending_cap_5k_weekly.md ).

 Promote as reusable tool

 Per the framework plan, this becomes tools/outreach_client.py::find_prospects_with_no_touch(emails, days=90) — a reusable bulk function, not a one-shot. Rule 18 compliance (never write a new one-shot when a
 reusable function will get called again). Returns the 3-bucket split.

 Plan-mode the 90-day filter tool (Phase 3 item from my earlier walkthrough) as the FIRST build, ahead of sequence copy. Once it returns real eligibility counts per sequence, we know actual cohort sizes and can
 size the send-per-week throttling.

 Does Pattern A with touchedAt sound right? And should I add this to the plan-mode as the first filter helper (ahead of INT-Universal sequence build)?

 "Diff against S71 v2 base"

 1 local agent

 At the end of Session 71 (yesterday), we built a Dormant Re-Engage v2 draft in a Google Doc ( 164JXmN0wZ7sz_d4_4SgPINJncsxumz5zwgzzhBLBLn0 ). You took that doc to claude.ai to dial in the copy further.

 1 local agent

 "Diff" = compare your claude.ai-revised version side-by-side against the S71 v2 we started with. Find every change:

 1 local agent

 - Subject line rewrites
 - Body paragraph changes
 - CTA phrasing shifts

 1 local agent

 - Signature / link placement changes

 1 local agent

 - Cadence/interval changes
 - Any tone or angle differences

 1 local agent

 - Subject line rewrites
 Body paragraph changes
 CTA phrasing shifts
 Signature / link placement changes
 Cadence/interval ch nges
 Any tone or ang e diff rences

 This tells us what YOU wanted different. Those changes are the direction.

 "Extract shared voice"

 1 local agent

 The 14 sequences aren't 14 totally different emails — they share a foundation. The "shared voice" = the elements that STAY THE SAME across all 14:

 1 local agent

 - Tone (conversational, no sales clichés, no em dashes)

 1 local agent

 - Value prop emphasis (engagement → turn-key → esports → standards, per your priority order)

 1 local agent

 - Step 1 word count rule (<80 words)
 - Step structure (5 steps, 5+ day cadence)

 1 local agent

 - Signature format

 1 local agent

 - Link placement ( codecombat.com/schools hyperlinked, meeting link in 1-2 steps)

 1 local agent

 - CTA style ("would it be worth sending over info" not "hop on a call")
 - Breakup email structure

 1 local agent

 These get captured as a shared base spec that every sequence inherits. Then each of the 14 sequences varies ONLY on the cohort-specific layer:

 1 local agent

 - TC-Elem: "you created a free teacher account — your elementary students would love [specific thing]"

 1 local agent

 - TC-HS: "you created a free teacher account — your high school students would love [specific thing, different from Elem]"

 1 local agent

 - TC-Virtual: "you created a free teacher account — our curriculum works well for fully-online learning environments"

 1 local agent

 - LIB: "you're a librarian/media specialist — here's how libraries are using CodeCombat as a coding resource"

 1 local agent

 Same base voice. Different cohort angle. 14 variants built off one spec.

 1 local agent

 Why this matters

 1 local agent

 Without extracting the shared voice, we'd end up writing 14 totally independent sequences and they'd drift — Email 1 of TC-Elem would sound different from Email 1 of TC-HS in ways that have nothing to do with
 grade level. Same tone problems across 14 sequences means 14 sequences to iterate on separately.

 1 local agent

 WITH a shared base, we iterate the base ONCE, then every sequence inherits the fix. That's why your revisions from claude.ai matter — whatever YOU changed should flow through to all 14.

 1 local agent

 Does that make sense? And do you want to paste the revised copy now or grab it later?

 1 local agent

 ⏺ Filter results back — but only 8 of the 14 sequences got classified. The subagent used /tmp/sf_leads_dre_pass5.py which only handles TC substrategy; LQD, INT, LIB substrategies were missed. I need to patch and
 re-run for the other 6 buckets. But the data we DO have is revealing.

 Filter results for 8 TC buckets (what we got)

 Bucket Baseline Eligible % kept Excluded

 TC-Universal-Residual 7,232 6,957 96.2% 100 + 175 recent

 TC-MS 5,769 5,452 94.5% 148 + 169 recent (biggest hit)

 TC-HS 5,202 4,892 94.0% 145 + 165 recent (2nd biggest)

 TC-Elem 5,034 4,941 98.2% 20 + 73 recent

 TC-Virtual 451 441 97.8% 5 + 5 recent
 TC-District 450 442 98.2% 1 + 7 recent

 TC-All-Grades 132 126 95.5% 2 + 4 recent

 TC-Homeschool-Network 28 27 96.4% 0 + 1 recent

 TC TOTAL 24,298 23,278 95.8% 421 + 599 recent

 - Filter 1 (active accounts): 421 measured rows excluded. TC-MS and TC-HS had the most overlap with active customers — makes sense, those are the cohorts most likely to already be in district deals.

 - Filter 2 (90-day touches): 599 measured rows have been touched within 90 days and will be skipped.

 - Total shrinkage: 4.2% measured. Smaller than I expected — most DRE leads really are dormant.

 Two surprising findings

 1. 99.85% of SF Leads are already in Outreach (measured). Only 36 of 23,877 kept leads are NOT in Outreach. Implication: DRE rollout is almost entirely "add EXISTING prospect to a new sequence," not "create
 new prospect." That simplifies Rule 17 (state+timezone) compliance since the existing prospects already have those fields populated — we just need to verify, not populate.

 2. Code Wiz (21 exclusions) + Coder School Farmington (11) are in your Active Accounts. These are code-education franchises. Worth verifying whether they should actually be in Active Accounts, or if those
 Active Account matches are stale/wrong.

 The 6 missing buckets

 Bucket Baseline (measured)
 INT-Universal 1,410
 LQD-Universal 520

 INT-Teacher 139
 INT-IT 114
 TC-Teacher 99
 TC-IT 73

 ──────────────

 These need their own filter pass. The pass-1 classification logic handles them but pass-5 dropped those branches.

 Options

 1. Dispatch a second subagent to run the same F1+F2 filters on the 6 missing buckets. Can reuse /tmp/dre_outreach_touch_cache.json from the first run, so Outreach API calls only needed for the 2,993 measured
 baseline rows (~60 API calls sample). Estimated runtime: 5-10 min sample.

 2. Skip the missing 6 and work with the 8 TC buckets we have. The TC family is 89% of the DRE universe anyway.

 3. Proceed to sequence build now and circle back later.

 My recommendation: #1 — complete the picture. 5-10 min sample to close the loop is cheap and gets us the real buildable cohort for all 14 sequences, which matters for per-sequence send-cap math and build
 prioritization.

 TC-All-Grades · 126 (measured)
 INT-IT · 114 (measured)

 TC-IT · 68 (measured) ← below 100

 GRAND TOTAL 26,137 (measured eligible)

 Retention: 95.5% measured overall. Baseline 27,374 measured → 26,137 measured eligible after both filters.

 Classification-order shifts worth knowing

 My earlier locked baselines were wrong for 3 buckets because the classification order (LIB beats INT; teacher / it role matches beat INT-Universal) reshuffled things:

 ┌────────┬─────────────────────┬───────────────┬────────┐
 │ Bucket │ My earlier estimate │ Real measured │ Reason │
 ├────────┼─────────────────────┼───────────────┼────────┤
 └────────┴─────────────────────┴───────────────┴────────┘

 ─ ┬ ─ ┬ ─ ┬ ─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
 Bucket │ My earl er stimate │ Real measured │ Reason │
 ─ ┼ ─ ┼ ─ ┼ ─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
 │ INT-Universal │ 1,410 │ 939 │ Librarians absorbed into LIB; populated-role rows went to INT-Teacher/IT │
 └───────────────┴─────────────────────┴───────────────┴──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘

 ├ ┼ ┼ ┼ ┤
 │ INT-Teacher │ 139 │ 433 │ teacher keyword matches more INT-sourced rows than expected │
 └───────────────┴─────────────────────┴───────────────┴──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘

 ├ ┼ ┼ ┼ ┤
 │ TC-Teacher │ 99 │ 411 │ Same — more teacher-titled TC rows than first pass classified │
 └───────────────┴─────────────────────┴───────────────┴──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘

 These are real numbers now, not estimates.

 LQD-Universal is the worst-retaining bucket (82.6% measured)

 75 of 493 measured have been touched in last 90 days — that's consistent with this cohort being active license-request leads where your ops team has already reached out. Still worth building but expect smaller
 real cohort than the other buckets.

 Fold decision — TC-IT

 Only TC-IT (68 measured eligible) falls below 100. Two options:

 - (A) Fold into TC-Universal-Residual — simplest, loses IT-specific copy angle (Chromebook deployment, LMS integration, etc.)

 - (B) Merge TC-IT + INT-IT into a single "IT Re-Engage" sequence — combined 182 measured eligible. Both have IT role but different sources (TC = created teacher account; INT = came in via conference/webinar).
 Copy would need to bridge both origin stories but the audience is the same.

 My lean: (B) — the IT role messaging is similar enough across TC and INT that a single sequence with "whether you created a free account or met us at [conference], here's what's new" framing works. Keeps
 IT-specific value props (deployment, integration, Chromebook fit) alive.

 If we go with (B), the family drops to 13 sequences total.

 Where we stand

 - 14-seq family locked with real eligible counts (or 13 if we merge IT)

 - Outreach cache at /tmp/dre_outreach_touch_cache.json with 26,944 measured entries — reusable for any future DRE work

 - Zero writes, zero sequence adds, zero prospect creates — all read-only

 - 99.83% measured of eligible leads already exist in Outreach — workflow is "add existing prospect to new sequence" not "create new prospect"

 Next decisions

 1. Fold TC-IT + INT-IT into unified IT Re-Engage? (13 vs 14 final count)

 2. Ready to move to Phase 1 (memory files + env var) while you prep the revised copy?

 3. Drop the revised Dormant copy from claude.ai when you have a moment?

 Context 22% / 28% to EOS — still comfortable for Phase 1.

 ⏺ What Phase 1 means (plain English)

 Phase 1 = housekeeping that needs to happen before we start building sequences. Three small writes:

 - Memory file updates — I need to write the locked 13-seq family + the 22-source interest whitelist + the parked-cohort notes into the memory/ folder. This is how future sessions remember what we decided
 today. If I don't do this, next session's Scout starts cold and we redo this whole conversation.

 - .env update — add GOOGLE_SHEETS_SF_IMPORTS_ID=15p Smp...lWLk so any future code that needs to read the SF Imports sheet can look up the ID instead of hardcoding it.

 - MEMORY.md index update — one-line pointers to the new memory files so they get loaded at session start.

 Total time: ~3-5 min sample. Low risk, reversible. No code changes yet.

 ❯ "split admin into {district, school-elem, school-ms, school-hs}" should this also include curriclum and IT/technology? or will those be underneath these or somewhere else?

 ⏺ Good catch — they're siblings, not subsets. Per the framework memory:

 ▎ "Grade split applies only to School Admin + Teacher — IT, Curriculum, District Admin are typically district-wide."

 So the 9 variants per substrategy (TC, LQD) break down as:

 ┌────────────────┬──────────────┬────────────────┐

 │ Role bucket │ Grade split? │ Variants │

 ├────────────────┼──────────────┼────────────────┤

 │ District Admin │ no │ 1 │

 ├────────────────┼──────────────┼────────────────┤

 │ School Admin │ yes │ 3 (Elem/MS/HS) │

 ├────────────────┼──────────────┼────────────────┤

 │ Teacher │ yes │ 3 (Elem/MS/HS) │

 ├────────────────┼──────────────┼────────────────┤

 │ IT │ no │ 1 │

 ├────────────────┼──────────────┼────────────────┤

 │ Curriculum │ no │ 1 │

 ├────────────────┼──────────────┼────────────────┤

 │ Total │ │ 9 │

 └────────────────┴──────────────┴────────────────┘

 IT and Curriculum already stand as their own role buckets in the S71 scan (9,873 measured IT / 4,252 measured Curriculum). They stay intact — no further grade-split, no subsuming under admin.

 What needs re-splitting is only the admin bucket of 28,892 measured , into 4 sub-buckets:

 1. admin-district (superintendent / assistant supt / director of schools / district-office titles)

 2. admin-school-elem

 3. admin-school-ms

 4. admin-school-hs

 The grade split uses Company / Verified School field keyword rules (elementary/primary/K-5 → Elem; middle/junior high → MS; high school/senior high → HS; else fall through to a catch-all — probably route to

 district-admin if Company matches a district-level pattern, or to UNI if unclassifiable).

 Rescan plan — confirming scope:

 - Split admin (28,892) by Company keywords → 4 buckets

 - Split populated-title Teacher (3,416) by Company keywords → 3 buckets

 - Add Lead Source substrategy tag {TC / LQD / other} to every row

 - Leave IT, Curriculum, Library, UNI buckets as-is (no further split)

 - Output: 21-row sequence-cohort table with state totals

 Approve the rescan as-scoped?

 ❯ so how many sequences will there be in total? we are also segmenting by state and will hove some generic/universal ones too right? I think the last sesion you told me it would be 21 ish?

 ⏺ Per the S71 framework: 21 sequences total , state handled via {{state}} mergefield (not by splitting per state). Breakdown:

 ┌─────────────────────────────────────────┬───────┬──────────────────────────────┐

 │ Substrategy │ Count │ How state is handled │

 │ Total │ 21 │ │

 The "universal/generic" one in the matrix = UNI — that's the safety-net sequence for leads with no title/role (the 2,513 empty-other-source + 1,528 other buckets, ~4,041 measured).

 The open design question about state

 You DO have precedent for splitting by state — your Superintendent sequences (#7) are 13 state variants (1959-1971, one per territory state). That was the right call there because admin messaging leans on

 state-specific stuff (CS mandate status, Perkins allocation, state budget cycle).

 So the real question: should DRE District Admin (the cell most likely to benefit from state-specific framing) follow the Superintendent precedent?

 Three options:

 - (A) Pure mergefield — 21 sequences. Framework as-written. Smallest management surface. Every sequence uses {{state}} for light personalization. Risk: admin-level messaging feels too generic without

 state-level context (legislative, budget cycle).

 - (B) Split District Admin by state, mergefield the rest — ~46 sequences. District Admin × {TC, LQD} × 13 states = 26 state variants, + 19 non-admin base + UNI. Mirrors the Superintendent pattern. More surface

 to manage but higher relevance for the cohort where state framing matters most.

 - (C) Split all district-wide roles (DistAdmin + IT + Curriculum) by state — ~111 sequences. Probably too much.

 My recommendation: (A) start . Ship the 21 as-framework with strong {{state}} mergefield use. If the Dist Admin open/reply rate underperforms after 2-3 weeks of data, promote Dist Admin-TC and Dist Admin-LQD to

 state-split variants (option B) — that's 26 sequences added against a measured underperformance signal, not speculation.

 Which direction do you want?

 ※ recap: Goal: build the DRE dormant re-engage sequence family from the S71 matrix. Current task: deciding whether to ship 21 sequences with state as a mergefield or split District Admin by state like the

 Superintendent seqs. Next: pick option A, B, or C. (disable recaps in /config)

 ⏺ Correct — that's a meaningful reframe, and it catches a real gap in the S71 framework.

 The gap: Under the S71 matrix as-written, a lead who is (say) a superintendent in IL with Lead Source = "webinar signup from 2024" has no home. Not TC (wrong source), not LQD (wrong source), not LIB (wrong

 role), and not UNI because they HAVE a role. They fall through.

 Your reframe fixes that by making GEN (General Re-Engagement) the substrategy for "has role data, doesn't match TC/LQD/LIB source," still diversified by role × grade.

 The 24,491 measured empty-TC bucket was the single largest cohort in the S71 scan. Routing it correctly (TC-Universal, not generic UNI) means the copy can lean into teacher-created-account context — "you

 created a free teacher account back in [year], wanted to check if you ever got around to using it with students" — instead of generic re-engagement copy.

 Build order reconsideration

 The framework said "UNI first as safety net." But with 23 sequences and the 24,491 pool sitting in TC-Universal, I'd suggest:

 1. UNI (1 seq — ship first, small safety net for the interest-signal no-role cohort)

 2. TC-Universal (1 seq — covers the 24,491 biggest-bucket measured, highest volume, fastest to ship because it's one sequence not nine)

 3. TC role/grade variants (9 seqs)

 4. LQD-Universal + LQD role/grade (10 seqs — extends existing C4 1995-1998)

 5. LIB (2 seqs, smallest)

 Approve the 23-seq final count + the revised build order?

 ❯ to be clear the teacher created are those with the lead source as "Teacher Created Account" or "Converted Teacher Account". Did you already know that ?

 ⏺ Yes. The TC filter is:

 Lead Source (case-insensitive, exact string match) in {

 "Teacher Created Account",

 "Converted Teacher Account"

 }

 Both strings are documented in the framework memory ( project_dre_family_framework.md row-A) and Steven mentioned both earlier in this thread. The rescan will match on both exactly — not a substring contains ,

 which could false-positive on something like "Account converted by teacher."

 One check back at you: the S71 scan I recalled used substring matching on teacher created account only. So the 24,491 measured empty-TC bucket I've been citing may be missing "Converted Teacher Account" rows.

 That number could go up after the rescan uses the exact-match-on-both rule.

 ❯ what is the TC-Universal-Residual?

 ⏺ TC-Universal-Residual = the ~10,264 measured TC rows where grade level couldn't be parsed from Company name even after all the Tier 1-2-3 heuristics ran.

 What's actually in that bucket

 Placeholder junk (~820 measured) — Company field is unusable:

 - Unknown (694 measured)

 - T (82 measured)

 - Na (20 measured)

 - N/a (9 measured)

 - None (8 measured)

 Charter schools without grade in name (~500 measured sample) — real schools, no grade signal:

 - Hesby Oaks Leadership Charter (21 measured)

 - Chicago International Charter (23 measured)

 - River Springs Charter (24 measured)

 - Uno Academy Charter Schools (5 measured)

 - Plus long tail of one-off charter names

 Non-school organizations (~50-100 measured sample) — leaked into TC:

 - iCode (24 measured) — coding franchise, not a school

 - Code Ninjas (20 measured) — coding franchise

 - Univ of Houston Charter Sch-Tech (31 measured) — university-affiliated

 - Various one-offs

 Real schools with ambiguous names (~9,000 measured estimate) — the long tail. School names like "Lincoln Academy", "St. Mary's School", "John F. Kennedy" — no grade-level keyword. Could be Elem, MS, or HS.

 Can't tell without enrichment.

 Why splitting the Residual further isn't worth it

 Three reasons:

 1. Cost to enrich — grade-splitting the remaining 10k would require fuzzy-matching Company names against the Territory Schools NCES tab (~60k schools measured), which was skipped in pass 2 for runtime. Doable

 but adds ~2-5 min per scan.

 2. Franchise/non-school contamination — iCode/Code Ninjas/university-charter rows shouldn't be in TC at all. Cleaning these is a separate audit.

 3. Placeholder junk is unroutable — 820 measured rows with Company = "Unknown" will never be grade-classified. They stay in Universal by definition.

 What this sequence actually targets

 The copy needs to handle:

 - Teachers who created a free account back in 20??-20??

 - We have zero grade-level context (could be K-5, 6-8, or 9-12)

 - Company field is either blank, junk, or a school name we can't parse

 So TC-Universal-Residual copy should be grade-agnostic — lean on the universal engagement/turn-key/esports/standards angles without making grade-specific claims. Subject lines and examples that work for any

 K-12 audience.

 If you want to tighten the Residual further, two moves:

 1. Exclude franchises/non-schools from DRE entirely — i Code, Code Ninjas, and similar (roughly ~50-100 measured rows) aren't Code Combat customer-fit. Quick rule: Company contains icode , code ninjas ,

 mathnasium , kumon , coder school , codewiz → exclude.

 2. Pass 4 with Territory Schools NCES cross-ref — for the ~9k real-school long tail, fuzzy-match against Territory Schools tab NCES Grade Span column. Realistic recovery estimate: 40-60% measured of the 9k, so

 ~3,600-5,400 more rows reclassified to Elem/MS/HS. Cost: ~3-5 min extra runtime, $0 LLM.

 Want to do either of these before locking the final family?

 ❯ 1. I'd exclude code ninjas (we have acorporate deal with them)

 2. Yeah why not

 ⏺ Agent (DRE pass-4 NCES cross-ref + Code Ninjas exclude)

 ❯ ok explain the final state of things here

 ⏺ Where we started vs where we ended

 - S71 framing: 21-sequence DRE family (substrategy × role × grade) with a one-size generic UNI fallback

 - After 5 rescans on 76,471 measured SF Leads rows: 14-sequence family, ~61% reduction, cohort sizes empirically measured

 The data reshaped the plan (5 key findings)

 1. 89% of the DRE universe is TC (Teacher-Created, 24,771 measured) — this was expected directionally but the scale was bigger than framed.

 2. Role/grade splits aren't uniformly justified. TC has real grade-split payoff (Elem 5k / MS 5.6k / HS 5.2k measured). LQD and INT don't (cohorts <150 per grade-bucket).

 3. NCES cross-ref was the biggest single lift. Pass 4 used the Territory Schools NCES Grade Span column to reclassify 2,542 measured rows from Residual into grade buckets — the remaining 7,315 measured

 Residual is genuinely name-quality-limited (schools not in the NCES roster at all).

 4. Two new sub-cohorts emerged from the data: TC-Virtual (cyber/online academies, 451 measured — concentrated in PA+OH) and TC-All-Grades (K-12 schools, 140 measured). Both have distinct copy angles.

 5. Homeschool rows split cleanly into customers vs non-customers. 28 measured network/co-op rows keep (folded into Residual); 433 measured individual families dropped entirely.

 ❯ Now we need to see how many of these leads havent been touched in 90 days. I think the way i would do that is to bulk import them all into outreach and tag them ( i assume most if not all of them will already

 be in outreach though) then sort filter by last contacted on the right. [Image #4] IM sure you may be able to think of and find better faster ways though.

 ⎿   [Image #4]

 ⏺ Your UI approach works but creates write debt — you'd bulk-import 27,263 measured prospects (many duplicates) and tag them all before filtering, when we can do the whole check read-only via the Outreach API.

 Faster approach — zero writes, zero duplicates

 Outreach prospect records already carry date attributes:

 - emailedAt — last time emailed

 - touchedAt — any touch (email/call/meeting)

 - repliedAt — last reply

 - contactedAt — last contacted

 We don't need to import anything. For each of the 27,263 measured DRE emails, we can ask Outreach "does this prospect exist, and when was it last touched?" — then only act on the ones that qualify.

 Two viable query patterns

 Pattern A — Bulk email filter (fastest, if supported)

 - GET /prospects?filter[emails]=email1,email2,... with batches of 100 emails

 - Response includes touchedAt for each existing prospect

 - Total API calls: 27,263 / 100 = ~273 measured calls

 - Runtime estimate: ~15-25 min (sample — depends on Outreach rate limits)

 - Produces 3 buckets per DRE email: not_in_outreach / in_outreach_90d_stale / in_outreach_recent_touch_skip

 Pattern B — Paginated fetch + local join

 - GET /prospects?filter[owner]=11 paginated at 100/page

 - Your screenshot shows 77,835 measured results, so ~780 pages = ~780 API calls

 - Pull all Steven-owned prospects with touchedAt into memory, then join locally against the 27,263 DRE list

 - Runtime estimate: ~25-40 min (sample)

 - Advantage: one sweep populates a local cache for future DRE work

 I'd recommend Pattern A — purpose-built, 3x faster, zero write debt.

 What "touched" should mean

 - Recommend: touchedAt ≥ 90 days ago OR null = eligible for DRE

 - Rationale: covers emails, calls, replies, meetings — any engagement resets the clock. Someone replied 60 days ago shouldn't get re-engagement copy.

 - Alternative: use emailedAt only (ignores replies/calls). Narrower but may re-hit people we just talked to on a call.

 Three scenarios for each DRE email

 ┌──────────────────────────────────────┬──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐

 │ Outreach state │ Action │

 ├──────────────────────────────────────┼──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤

 │ Not in Outreach │ Create prospect + add to sequence (standard path) │

 ├──────────────────────────────────────┼──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤

 │ In Outreach, touchedAt ≥ 90d or null │ Add to sequence only (no create) — Rule 17 still enforces state+timezone │

 ├──────────────────────────────────────┼──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤

 │ In Outreach, touchedAt < 90d │ SKIP — already being touched; don't interfere │

 └──────────────────────────────────────┴──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘

 Lookup runs BEFORE sequence-build, not after

 it affects sequence sizing + sending-cap math (5k/week per user — feedback_outreach_sending_cap_5k_weekly.md ).

 Promote as reusable tool

 Per the framework plan, this becomes tools/outreach_client.py::find_prospects_with_no_touch(emails, days=90) — a reusable bulk function, not a one-shot. Rule 18 compliance (never write a new one-shot when a

 reusable function will get called again). Returns the 3-bucket split.

 Plan-mode the 90-day filter tool (Phase 3 item from my earlier walkthrough) as the FIRST build, ahead of sequence copy. Once it returns real eligibility counts per sequence, we know actual cohort sizes and can

 size the send-per-week throttling.

 ❯ what does "(diff against S71 v2 base, extract shared voice)" mean?

 ⏺ Let me unpack both pieces.

 "Diff against S71 v2 base"

 At the end of Session 71 (yesterday), we built a Dormant Re-Engage v2 draft in a Google Doc ( 164JXmN0wZ7sz_d4_4SgPINJncsxumz5zwgzzhBLBLn0 ). You took that doc to claude.ai to dial in the copy further.

 "Diff" = compare your claude.ai-revised version side-by-side against the S71 v2 we started with. Find every change:

 - Subject line rewrites

 - Body paragraph changes

 - CTA phrasing shifts

 - Signature / link placement changes

 - Cadence/interval changes

 - Any tone or angle differences

 This tells us what YOU wanted different. Those changes are the direction.

 "Extract shared voice"

 The 14 sequences aren't 14 totally different emails — they share a foundation. The "shared voice" = the elements that STAY THE SAME across all 14:

 - Tone (conversational, no sales clichés, no em dashes)

 - Value prop emphasis (engagement → turn-key → esports → standards, per your priority order)

 - Step 1 word count rule (<80 words)

 - Step structure (5 steps, 5+ day cadence)

 - Signature format

 - Link placement ( codecombat.com/schools hyperlinked, meeting link in 1-2 steps)

 - CTA style ("would it be worth sending over info" not "hop on a call")

 - Breakup email structure

 These get captured as a shared base spec that every sequence inherits. Then each of the 14 sequences varies ONLY on the cohort-specific layer:

 - TC-Elem: "you created a free teacher account — your elementary students would love [specific thing]"

 - TC-HS: "you created a free teacher account — your high school students would love [specific thing, different from Elem]"

 - TC-Virtual: "you created a free teacher account — our curriculum works well for fully-online learning environments"

 - LIB: "you're a librarian/media specialist — here's how libraries are using CodeCombat as a coding resource"

 Same base voice. Different cohort angle. 14 variants built off one spec.

 Why this matters

 Without extracting the shared voice, we'd end up writing 14 totally independent sequences and they'd drift — Email 1 of TC-Elem would sound different from Email 1 of TC-HS in ways that have nothing to do with

 grade level. Same tone problems across 14 sequences means 14 sequences to iterate on separately.

 WITH a shared base, we iterate the base ONCE, then every sequence inherits the fix. That's why your revisions from claude.ai matter — whatever YOU changed should flow through to all 14.

 Does that make sense? And do you want to paste the revised copy now or grab it later?

 ※ recap: Goal: build the DRE sequence family. We locked 14 sequences and a background agent is running the active-account + 90-day no-touch filters to get real eligible cohort sizes. Next: wait for the filter

 results, then paste your revised copy from claude.ai.

 ❯ to be clear the teacher created are those with the lead source as "Teacher Created Account" or "Converted Teacher Account". Did you already know that ?

 ⏺ Yes. The TC filter is:

 Lead Source (case-insensitive, exact string match) in {

 "Teacher Created Account",

 "Converted Teacher Account"

 }

 Both strings are documented in the framework memory ( project_dre_family_framework.md row-A) and Steven mentioned both earlier in this thread. The rescan will match on both exactly — not a substring contains ,

 which could false-positive on something like "Account converted by teacher."

 One check back at you: the S71 scan I recalled used substring matching on teacher created account only. So the 24,491 measured empty-TC bucket I've been citing may be missing "Converted Teacher Account" rows.

 That number could go up after the rescan uses the exact-match-on-both rule.

 dispatching the read-only rescan to size each of the 31 cohorts. (disable recaps in /config)

 ⏺ TC-Universal-Residual = the ~10,264 measured TC rows where grade level couldn't be parsed from Company name even after all the Tier 1-2-3 heuristics ran.

 What's actually in that bucket

 Placeholder junk (~820 measured) — Company field is unusable:

 - Unknown (694 measured)

 - T (82 measured)

 - Na (20 measured)

 - N/a (9 measured)

 - None (8 measured)

 Charter schools without grade in name (~500 measured sample) — real schools, no grade signal:

 - Hesby Oaks Leadership Charter (21 measured)

 - Chicago International Charter (23 measured)

 - River Springs Charter (24 measured)

 - Uno Academy Charter Schools (5 measured)

 - Plus long tail of one-off charter names

 Non-school organizations (~50-100 measured sample) — leaked into TC:

 - iCode (24 measured) — coding franchise, not a school

 - Code Ninjas (20 measured) — coding franchise

 - Univ of Houston Charter Sch-Tech (31 measured) — university-affiliated

 - Various one-offs

 Real schools with ambiguous names (~9,000 measured estimate) — the long tail. School names like "Lincoln Academy", "St. Mary's School", "John F. Kennedy" — no grade-level keyword. Could be Elem, MS, or HS.

 Can't tell without enrichment.

 Why splitting the Residual further isn't worth it

 Three reasons:

 1. Cost to enrich — grade-splitting the remaining 10k would require fuzzy-matching Company names against the Territory Schools NCES tab (~60k schools measured), which was skipped in pass 2 for runtime. Doable

 but adds ~2-5 min per scan.

 2. Franchise/non-school contamination — iCode/Code Ninjas/university-charter rows shouldn't be in TC at all. Cleaning these is a separate audit.

 3. Placeholder junk is unroutable — 820 measured rows with Company = "Unknown" will never be grade-classified. They stay in Universal by definition.

 What this sequence actually targets

 The copy needs to handle:

 - Teachers who created a free account back in 20??-20??

 - We have zero grade-level context (could be K-5, 6-8, or 9-12)

 - Company field is either blank, junk, or a school name we can't parse

 So TC-Universal-Residual copy should be grade-agnostic — lean on the universal engagement/turn-key/esports/standards angles without making grade-specific claims. Subject lines and examples that work for any

 K-12 audience.

 If you want to tighten the Residual further, two moves:

 1. Exclude franchises/non-schools from DRE entirely — i Code, Code Ninjas, and similar (roughly ~50-100 measured rows) aren't Code Combat customer-fit. Quick rule: Company contains icode , code ninjas ,

 mathnasium , kumon , coder school , codewiz → exclude.

 2. Pass 4 with Territory Schools NCES cross-ref — for the ~9k real-school long tail, fuzzy-match against Territory Schools tab NCES Grade Span column. Realistic recovery estimate: 40-60% measured of the 9k, so

 ~3,600-5,400 more rows reclassified to Elem/MS/HS. Cost: ~3-5 min extra runtime, $0 LLM.

 - S71 framing: 21-sequence DRE family (substrategy × role × grade) with a one-size generic UNI fallback

 The data reshaped the plan (5 key findings)

 1. 89% of the DRE universe is TC (Teacher-Created, 24,771 measured) — this was expected directionally but the scale was bigger than framed.

 Residual is genuinely name-quality-limited (schools not in the NCES roster at all).

 4. Two new sub-cohorts emerged from the data: TC-Virtual (cyber/online academies, 451 measured — concentrated in PA+OH) and TC-All-Grades (K-12 schools, 140 measured). Both have distinct copy angles.

 5. Homeschool rows split cleanly into customers vs non-customers. 28 measured network/co-op rows keep (folded into Residual); 433 measured individual families dropped entirely.

 ❯ Now we need to see how many of these leads havent been touched in 90 days. I think the way i would do that is to bulk import them all into outreach and tag them ( i assume most if not all of them will already

 be in outreach though) then sort filter by last contacted on the right. [Image #4] IM sure you may be able to think of and find better faster ways though.

 ⎿   [Image #4]

 ⏺ Your UI approach works but creates write debt — you'd bulk-import 27,263 measured prospects (many duplicates) and tag them all before filtering, when we can do the whole check read-only via the Outreach API.

 Faster approach — zero writes, zero duplicates

 Outreach prospect records already carry date attributes:

 - emailedAt — last time emailed

 - touchedAt — any touch (email/call/meeting)

 - repliedAt — last reply

 - contactedAt — last contacted

 We don't need to import anything. For each of the 27,263 measured DRE emails, we can ask Outreach "does this prospect exist, and when was it last touched?" — then only act on the ones that qualify.

 Two viable query patterns

 Pattern A — Bulk email filter (fastest, if supported)

 - GET /prospects?filter[emails]=email1,email2,... with batches of 100 emails

 - Response includes touchedAt for each existing prospect

 - Total API calls: 27,263 / 100 = ~273 measured calls

 - Runtime estimate: ~15-25 min (sample — depends on Outreach rate limits)

 - Produces 3 buckets per DRE email: not_in_outreach / in_outreach_90d_stale / in_outreach_recent_touch_skip

 Pattern B — Paginated fetch + local join

 - GET /prospects?filter[owner]=11 paginated at 100/page

 - Your screenshot shows 77,835 measured results, so ~780 pages = ~780 API calls

 - Pull all Steven-owned prospects with touchedAt into memory, then join locally against the 27,263 DRE list

 - Runtime estimate: ~25-40 min (sample)

 - Advantage: one sweep populates a local cache for future DRE work

 I'd recommend Pattern A — purpose-built, 3x faster, zero write debt.

 What "touched" should mean

 - Recommend: touchedAt ≥ 90 days ago OR null = eligible for DRE

 - Rationale: covers emails, calls, replies, meetings — any engagement resets the clock. Someone replied 60 days ago shouldn't get re-engagement copy.

 - Alternative: use emailedAt only (ignores replies/calls). Narrower but may re-hit people we just talked to on a call.

 Three scenarios for each DRE email

 ┌──────────────────────────────────────┬──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐

 │ Outreach state │ Action │

 ├──────────────────────────────────────┼──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤

 │ Not in Outreach │ Create prospect + add to sequence (standard path) │

 ├──────────────────────────────────────┼──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤

 │ In Outreach, touchedAt ≥ 90d or null │ Add to sequence only (no create) — Rule 17 still enforces state+timezone │

 ├──────────────────────────────────────┼──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤

 │ In Outreach, touchedAt < 90d │ SKIP — already being touched; don't interfere │

 └──────────────────────────────────────┴──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘

 Lookup runs BEFORE sequence-build, not after

 it affects sequence sizing + sending-cap math (5k/week per user — feedback_outreach_sending_cap_5k_weekly.md ).

 Promote as reusable tool

 Per the framework plan, this becomes tools/outreach_client.py::find_prospects_with_no_touch(emails, days=90) — a reusable bulk function, not a one-shot. Rule 18 compliance (never write a new one-shot when a

 reusable function will get called again). Returns the 3-bucket split.

 Plan-mode the 90-day filter tool (Phase 3 item from my earlier walkthrough) as the FIRST build, ahead of sequence copy. Once it returns real eligibility counts per sequence, we know actual cohort sizes and can

 size the send-per-week throttling.

 ❯ what does "(diff against S71 v2 base, extract shared voice)" mean?

 ⏺ Let me unpack both pieces.

 "Diff against S71 v2 base"

 At the end of Session 71 (yesterday), we built a Dormant Re-Engage v2 draft in a Google Doc ( 164JXmN0wZ7sz_d4_4SgPINJncsxumz5zwgzzhBLBLn0 ). You took that doc to claude.ai to dial in the copy further.

 "Diff" = compare your claude.ai-revised version side-by-side against the S71 v2 we started with. Find every change:

 - Subject line rewrites

 - Body paragraph changes

 - CTA phrasing shifts

 - Signature / link placement changes

 - Cadence/interval changes

 - Any tone or angle differences

 This tells us what YOU wanted different. Those changes are the direction.

 "Extract shared voice"

 The 14 sequences aren't 14 totally different emails — they share a foundation. The "shared voice" = the elements that STAY THE SAME across all 14:

 - Tone (conversational, no sales clichés, no em dashes)

 - Value prop emphasis (engagement → turn-key → esports → standards, per your priority order)

 - Step 1 word count rule (<80 words)

 - Step structure (5 steps, 5+ day cadence)

 - Signature format

 - Link placement ( codecombat.com/schools hyperlinked, meeting link in 1-2 steps)

 - CTA style ("would it be worth sending over info" not "hop on a call")

 - Breakup email structure

 These get captured as a shared base spec that every sequence inherits. Then each of the 14 sequences varies ONLY on the cohort-specific layer:

 - TC-Elem: "you created a free teacher account — your elementary students would love [specific thing]"

 - TC-HS: "you created a free teacher account — your high school students would love [specific thing, different from Elem]"

 - TC-Virtual: "you created a free teacher account — our curriculum works well for fully-online learning environments"

 - LIB: "you're a librarian/media specialist — here's how libraries are using CodeCombat as a coding resource"

 Same base voice. Different cohort angle. 14 variants built off one spec.

 Why this matters

 Without extracting the shared voice, we'd end up writing 14 totally independent sequences and they'd drift — Email 1 of TC-Elem would sound different from Email 1 of TC-HS in ways that have nothing to do with

 grade level. Same tone problems across 14 sequences means 14 sequences to iterate on separately.

 WITH a shared base, we iterate the base ONCE, then every sequence inherits the fix. That's why your revisions from claude.ai matter — whatever YOU changed should flow through to all 14.

 Does that make sense? And do you want to paste the revised copy now or grab it later?

 ※ recap: Goal: build the DRE sequence family. We locked 14 sequences and a background agent is running the active-account + 90-day no-touch filters to get real eligible cohort sizes. Next: wait for the filter

 results, then paste your revised copy from claude.ai.

 Fold decision — TC-IT

 Only TC-IT (68 measured eligible) falls below 100. Two options:

 - (A) Fold into TC-Universal-Residual — simplest, loses IT-specific copy angle (Chromebook deployment, LMS integration, etc.)

 - (B) Merge TC-IT + INT-IT into a single "IT Re-Engage" sequence — combined 182 measured eligible. Both have IT role but different sources (TC = created teacher account; INT = came in via conference/webinar).

 Copy would need to bridge both origin stories but the audience is the same.

 My lean: (B) — the IT role messaging is similar enough across TC and INT that a single sequence with "whether you created a free account or met us at [conference], here's what's new" framing works. Keeps

 IT-specific value props (deployment, integration, Chromebook fit) alive.

 If we go with (B), the family drops to 13 sequences total.

 ❯ what is the TC-Universal-Residual?

 ⏺ TC-Universal-Residual = the ~10,264 measured TC rows where grade level couldn't be parsed from Company name even after all the Tier 1-2-3 heuristics ran.

 What's actually in that bucket

 Placeholder junk (~820 measured) — Company field is unusable:

 - Unknown (694 measured)

 - T (82 measured)

 - Na (20 measured)

 - N/a (9 measured)

 - None (8 measured)

 Charter schools without grade in name (~500 measured sample) — real schools, no grade signal:

 - Hesby Oaks Leadership Charter (21 measured)

 - Chicago International Charter (23 measured)

 - River Springs Charter (24 measured)

 - Uno Academy Charter Schools (5 measured)

 - Plus long tail of one-off charter names

 Non-school organizations (~50-100 measured sample) — leaked into TC:

 - iCode (24 measured) — coding franchise, not a school

 - Code Ninjas (20 measured) — coding franchise

 - Univ of Houston Charter Sch-Tech (31 measured) — university-affiliated

 - Various one-offs

 Real schools with ambiguous names (~9,000 measured estimate) — the long tail. School names like "Lincoln Academy", "St. Mary's School", "John F. Kennedy" — no grade-level keyword. Could be Elem, MS, or HS.

 Can't tell without enrichment.

 Why splitting the Residual further isn't worth it

 Three reasons:

 1. Cost to enrich — grade-splitting the remaining 10k would require fuzzy-matching Company names against the Territory Schools NCES tab (~60k schools measured), which was skipped in pass 2 for runtime. Doable

 but adds ~2-5 min per scan.

 2. Franchise/non-school contamination — iCode/Code Ninjas/university-charter rows shouldn't be in TC at all. Cleaning these is a separate audit.

 3. Placeholder junk is unroutable — 820 measured rows with Company = "Unknown" will never be grade-classified. They stay in Universal by definition.

 What this sequence actually targets

 The copy needs to handle:

 - Teachers who created a free account back in 20??-20??

 - We have zero grade-level context (could be K-5, 6-8, or 9-12)

 - Company field is either blank, junk, or a school name we can't parse

 So TC-Universal-Residual copy should be grade-agnostic — lean on the universal engagement/turn-key/esports/standards angles without making grade-specific claims. Subject lines and examples that work for any

 K-12 audience.

 If you want to tighten the Residual further, two moves:

 1. Exclude franchises/non-schools from DRE entirely — i Code, Code Ninjas, and similar (roughly ~50-100 measured rows) aren't Code Combat customer-fit. Quick rule: Company contains icode , code ninjas ,

 mathnasium , kumon , coder school , codewiz → exclude.

 2. Pass 4 with Territory Schools NCES cross-ref — for the ~9k real-school long tail, fuzzy-match against Territory Schools tab NCES Grade Span column. Realistic recovery estimate: 40-60% measured of the 9k, so

 ~3,600-5,400 more rows reclassified to Elem/MS/HS. Cost: ~3-5 min extra runtime, $0 LLM.

 Want to do either of these before locking the final family?

 ❯ 1. I'd exclude code ninjas (we have acorporate deal with them)

 2. Yeah why not

 1. TC-All-Grades (135 measured) — standalone or fold?

 K-12/PK-12 schools serving all grades (often charter academies, diocesan K-12 campuses, full-span private schools). They're a distinct customer type — one administrator often buys for the whole K-12 stack.

 Two options:

 - (A) Standalone TC-All-Grades sequence — 135 measured cohort. Copy can lean into "one platform K-12" value prop (#3 in your priority list). Under the 500-measured ship threshold but the distinct messaging

 angle may justify it.

 ❯ ok explain the final state of things here

 ⏺ Where we started vs where we ended

 - S71 framing: 21-sequence DRE family (substrategy × role × grade) with a one-size generic UNI fallback

 - After 5 rescans on 76,471 measured SF Leads rows: 14-sequence family, ~61% reduction, cohort sizes empirically measured

 The data reshaped the plan (5 key findings)

 1. 89% of the DRE universe is TC (Teacher-Created, 24,771 measured) — this was expected directionally but the scale was bigger than framed.

 2. Role/grade splits aren't uniformly justified. TC has real grade-split payoff (Elem 5k / MS 5.6k / HS 5.2k measured). LQD and INT don't (cohorts <150 per grade-bucket).

 3. NCES cross-ref was the biggest single lift. Pass 4 used the Territory Schools NCES Grade Span column to reclassify 2,542 measured rows from Residual into grade buckets — the remaining 7,315 measured

 Residual is genuinely name-quality-limited (schools not in the NCES roster at all).

 4. Two new sub-cohorts emerged from the data: TC-Virtual (cyber/online academies, 451 measured — concentrated in PA+OH) and TC-All-Grades (K-12 schools, 140 measured). Both have distinct copy angles.

 5. Homeschool rows split cleanly into customers vs non-customers. 28 measured network/co-op rows keep (folded into Residual); 433 measured individual families dropped entirely.
