 ❯ Now we need to see how many of these leads havent been touched in 90 days. I think the way i would do that is to bulk import them all into outreach and tag them ( i assume most if not all of them will already

 be in outreach though) then sort filter by last contacted on the right. [Image #4] IM sure you may be able to think of and find better faster ways though.

 ⎿   [Image #4]

 ⏺ Your UI approach works but creates write debt — you'd bulk-import 27,263 measured prospects (many duplicates) and tag them all before filtering, when we can do the whole check read-only via the Outreach API.

 Faster approach — zero writes, zero duplicates

 Outreach prospect records already carry date attributes:

 - emailedAt — last time emailed

 - touchedAt — any touch (email/call/meeting)

 - repliedAt — last reply

 - contactedAt — last contacted

 We don't need to import anything. For each of the 27,263 measured DRE emails, we can ask Outreach "does this prospect exist, and when was it last touched?" — then only act on the ones that qualify.

 Two viable query patterns

 Pattern A — Bulk email filter (fastest, if supported)

 - GET /prospects?filter[emails]=email1,email2,... with batches of 100 emails

 - Response includes touchedAt for each existing prospect

 - Total API calls: 27,263 / 100 = ~273 measured calls

 - Runtime estimate: ~15-25 min (sample — depends on Outreach rate limits)

 - Produces 3 buckets per DRE email: not_in_outreach / in_outreach_90d_stale / in_outreach_recent_touch_skip

 Pattern B — Paginated fetch + local join

 - GET /prospects?filter[owner]=11 paginated at 100/page

 - Your screenshot shows 77,835 measured results, so ~780 pages = ~780 API calls

 - Pull all Steven-owned prospects with touchedAt into memory, then join locally against the 27,263 DRE list

 - Runtime estimate: ~25-40 min (sample)

 - Advantage: one sweep populates a local cache for future DRE work

 I'd recommend Pattern A — purpose-built, 3x faster, zero write debt.

 What "touched" should mean

 - Recommend: touchedAt ≥ 90 days ago OR null = eligible for DRE

 - Rationale: covers emails, calls, replies, meetings — any engagement resets the clock. Someone replied 60 days ago shouldn't get re-engagement copy.

 - Alternative: use emailedAt only (ignores replies/calls). Narrower but may re-hit people we just talked to on a call.

 Three scenarios for each DRE email

 ┌──────────────────────────────────────┬──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐

 │ Outreach state │ Action │

 ├──────────────────────────────────────┼──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤

 │ Not in Outreach │ Create prospect + add to sequence (standard path) │

 ├──────────────────────────────────────┼──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤

 │ In Outreach, touchedAt ≥ 90d or null │ Add to sequence only (no create) — Rule 17 still enforces state+timezone │

 ├──────────────────────────────────────┼──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤

 │ In Outreach, touchedAt < 90d │ SKIP — already being touched; don't interfere │

 └──────────────────────────────────────┴──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘

 Lookup runs BEFORE sequence-build, not after

 it affects sequence sizing + sending-cap math (5k/week per user — feedback_outreach_sending_cap_5k_weekly.md ).

 Promote as reusable tool

 Per the framework plan, this becomes tools/outreach_client.py::find_prospects_with_no_touch(emails, days=90) — a reusable bulk function, not a one-shot. Rule 18 compliance (never write a new one-shot when a

 reusable function will get called again). Returns the 3-bucket split.

 Plan-mode the 90-day filter tool (Phase 3 item from my earlier walkthrough) as the FIRST build, ahead of sequence copy. Once it returns real eligibility counts per sequence, we know actual cohort sizes and can

 size the send-per-week throttling.

 ❯ what does "(diff against S71 v2 base, extract shared voice)" mean?

 ⏺ Let me unpack both pieces.

 "Diff against S71 v2 base"

 At the end of Session 71 (yesterday), we built a Dormant Re-Engage v2 draft in a Google Doc ( 164JXmN0wZ7sz_d4_4SgPINJncsxumz5zwgzzhBLBLn0 ). You took that doc to claude.ai to dial in the copy further.

 "Diff" = compare your claude.ai-revised version side-by-side against the S71 v2 we started with. Find every change:

 - Subject line rewrites

 - Body paragraph changes

 - CTA phrasing shifts

 - Signature / link placement changes

 - Cadence/interval changes

 - Any tone or angle differences

 This tells us what YOU wanted different. Those changes are the direction.

 "Extract shared voice"

 The 14 sequences aren't 14 totally different emails — they share a foundation. The "shared voice" = the elements that STAY THE SAME across all 14:

 - Tone (conversational, no sales clichés, no em dashes)

 - Value prop emphasis (engagement → turn-key → esports → standards, per your priority order)

 - Step 1 word count rule (<80 words)

 - Step structure (5 steps, 5+ day cadence)

 - Signature format

 - Link placement ( codecombat.com/schools hyperlinked, meeting link in 1-2 steps)

 - CTA style ("would it be worth sending over info" not "hop on a call")

 - Breakup email structure

 These get captured as a shared base spec that every sequence inherits. Then each of the 14 sequences varies ONLY on the cohort-specific layer:

 - TC-Elem: "you created a free teacher account — your elementary students would love [specific thing]"

 - TC-HS: "you created a free teacher account — your high school students would love [specific thing, different from Elem]"

 - TC-Virtual: "you created a free teacher account — our curriculum works well for fully-online learning environments"

 - LIB: "you're a librarian/media specialist — here's how libraries are using CodeCombat as a coding resource"

 Same base voice. Different cohort angle. 14 variants built off one spec.

 Why this matters

 Without extracting the shared voice, we'd end up writing 14 totally independent sequences and they'd drift — Email 1 of TC-Elem would sound different from Email 1 of TC-HS in ways that have nothing to do with

 grade level. Same tone problems across 14 sequences means 14 sequences to iterate on separately.

 WITH a shared base, we iterate the base ONCE, then every sequence inherits the fix. That's why your revisions from claude.ai matter — whatever YOU changed should flow through to all 14.

 Does that make sense? And do you want to paste the revised copy now or grab it later?

 ※ recap: Goal: build the DRE sequence family. We locked 14 sequences and a background agent is running the active-account + 90-day no-touch filters to get real eligible cohort sizes. Next: wait for the filter

 results, then paste your revised copy from claude.ai.

 ⏺ DRE Sequence Family — How We Got to 13

 [<u[>1u[>4;2m

 Session 72, 2026-04-16 . Walkthrough of the reasoning, the data, and the decisions that collapsed yesterday's 21-sequence theoretical framework into today's 13-sequence data-backed family.

 ---

 Built a 21-sequence DRE framework organized as a substrategy × role × grade matrix :

 - TC (Teacher-Created free accounts): 9 variants = Dist-Admin + Sch-Admin × 3 grades + Teacher × 3 grades + IT + Curriculum
 - LQD (License/Quote/Demo requests): 9 variants (same matrix)

 - LIB (Library/Librarian): 2 variants
 - UNI (Universal Fallback, no role): 1 variant

 21 total. The problem: it was theoretical. We hadn't counted leads per bucket. We didn't know if the grade splits were justified or if we'd be building empty sequences.

 Today's work — let data reshape the plan

 Ran 5 classification passes on 76,471 measured SF Leads rows, then 2 filter passes.

 Pass 1 — baseline classification

 Full universe breakdown by role:

 admin 28,892 (measured — 37.78%)
 empty-title TC 24,491 (measured — 32.03%)

 IT 9,873 (measured — 12.91%)
 curriculum 4,252 (measured — 5.56%)

 teacher 3,416 (measured — 4.47%)
 empty-title other 2,513 (measured — 3.29%)

 other/unmatched 1,528 (measured — 2.00%)

 admin-support 1,106 (measured — 1.45%)
 library 379 (measured — 0.50%)

 Pass 2 — grade inference on the two biggest universals

 Attempted keyword-based grade detection from Company field on TC-Universal (25,167 measured) and INT-Universal (1,410 measured).

 TC-Universal split cleanly. Elem 3,657 / MS 4,809 / HS 4,342 / District 364 / Residual 11,593 — all measured. Three grade buckets well above any ship threshold.

 INT-Universal did NOT split cleanly. All grade cohorts came in under 100 measured. Forcing a grade split would create near-empty sequences.

 → First reframe: INT stays as a single Universal, not 9 variants. TC gets grade-split.

 [<u[>1u[>4;2m

 Pass 3 — rule tweaks + new buckets surfaced from the data

 Four rule additions:

 - Standalone unified → District bucket (recovered 88 LAUSD-style measured rows)
 - Trailing ms abbreviation → MS bucket (recovered 335 measured rows)

 - Virtual/Cyber/Online academy → new TC-Virtual bucket (451 measured, concentrated in PA+OH cyber-charter states)

 - Homeschool → split into TC-Homeschool-Network (28 measured, borderline) and TC-Homeschool-Excluded (433 measured individual family accounts, dropped as non-customers)

 - Standalone unified → District bucket (recovered 88 LAUSD-style measured rows)
 Tr iling ms abbreviat on → MS bucket (recovered 335 measured rows)
 Virtual/Cyber/Online academy → new TC-Virtual bucket (451 m asured, concentrated in PA+OH cyber-charter states)
 Homeschool → split into TC-Homeschool Network (28 measured, bord rline) a d TC-Homeschool-Excluded (433 me sured individual family accounts, dropped as non-customers)

 → Second reframe: Three buckets the original matrix didn't anticipate — TC-Virtual, TC-District, TC-All-Grades — emerged because the data structure had them.

 Pass 4 — NCES cross-reference (biggest single lift)

 Fuzzy-matched the 10,264 measured "residual" Company names against the Territory Schools tab (~60,000 measured schools) and lifted NCES Grade Span authoritative grade assignments. Recovered 2,542 measured rows
 from Residual into Elem/MS/HS buckets. Also surfaced 135 measured K-12 schools as TC-All-Grades (a new bucket).

 Pass 5 — state-aware disambiguation (final sweep)

 Ran state-filtering on the 1,699 measured "ambiguous" matches (common school names like "Lincoln Elementary" that exist in 5+ states). Recovered only 367 measured rows. Remaining residual is
 name-quality-limited — schools genuinely not in the NCES roster. Stopped enriching.

 Filter 1 — active account cross-check

 Cross-referenced every DRE lead's Company against the Active Accounts tab. Excluded leads where:

 - Fuzzy match to active account with Deal Level = district (CSMs handle)

 - Exact match to an active account at school level

 - Fuzzy match to active account with Deal Level = district (CSMs handle)
 Exact n active account at school level

 421 measured rows excluded. Bulk of exclusions were TC-MS and TC-HS, where active-customer overlap is highest.

 Filter 2 — 90-day Outreach no-touch

 Bulk-queried Outreach for every DRE email's touchedAt timestamp (478 measured API calls, 7 min wall). Bucketed into:

 - Not in Outreach (36 measured — these need prospect creation)

 - In Outreach, stale ≥90 days (25,991 measured — eligible for DRE)

 - In Outreach, touched <90 days (780 measured — skip, already being engaged)

 - Not in Outreach (36 measured — these need prospect creation)
 In Outreach, stale ≥90 days (25,991 measured — ligible f r DRE)
 touched <90 days (780 measured — skip, a ready being engaged)

 99.83% measured of eligible leads already exist in Outreach. Workflow is "add existing prospect to new sequence," not "create new prospect." Rule 17 (state + timezone) compliance is mostly verification, not
 population.

 1. GEN substrategy parked. When I proposed a "General Re-Engagement" substrategy for role-populated leads outside TC/LQD/LIB source whitelists, you caught that it belongs in cold outreach, not dormant
 re-engagement. ~48,000 measured rows (Zen Prospect/Agile/MCH/Gov Spend/K12Prospects) parked for a future cold-email session.

 2. UNI tightened to 22 interest-signal sources. Instead of routing any empty-title lead to UNI, you defined UNI as empty-title leads with a clear interest-signal Lead Source (conference, webinar, Hour of Code,
 Drift/Intercom chat, etc.). Prevents bought leads from getting dormant-re-engagement copy.

 3. Each substrategy gets its own Universal variant. TC-Universal for empty-title TC leads, LQD-Universal for empty-title LQD leads, INT-Universal for empty-title INT leads. One generic UNI would have mixed
 source contexts incorrectly.

 4. LIB collapsed 2 → 1. You flagged that 2 variants was overkill for 638 measured librarians.

 5. State-per-sequence not justified. Your Superintendent #7 sequences are state-split (13 variants) because admin messaging leans on state-specific legislative/budget context. DRE doesn't — {{state}}
 mergefield covers the personalization need. Confirmed option A (mergefield, not split).

 6. Code Ninjas excluded. 40 measured rows, you have a corporate deal.

 7. Homeschool individual families excluded. 433 measured rows, not customer-fit.

 8. TC-IT + INT-IT merged into IT-ReEngage. Each was below 200 measured alone; merged = 182 measured. IT messaging bridges both origin stories (Chromebook deployment, LMS integration).

 Final family (13 sequences, 26,137 measured eligible leads)

 Eligible % of DRE

 TC-Universal-Residual 6,957 26.6%

 TC-MS 5,452 20.9%
 TC-HS 4,892 18.7%

 TC-Elem 4,941 18.9%
 INT-Universal 867 3.3%

 LIB 633 2.4%
 TC-Virtual 441 1.7%

 TC-District 442 1.7%
 LQD-Universal 407 1.6%

 INT-Teacher 404 1.5%
 TC-Teacher 393 1.5%

 IT-ReEngage 182 0.7%
 TC-All-Grades 126 0.5%

 Key takeaways

 1. TC dominates the DRE universe — 89% measured of all eligible leads. The Teacher-Created free-account cohort is by far the biggest re-engagement target.

 2. The S71 matrix was over-engineered. Theoretical role × grade × substrategy splits produced dozens of near-empty buckets. Real data supports 13 variants, not 21 (and not the ~60 the fully-expanded matrix
 would have produced).

 3. NCES Grade Span enrichment was the single biggest lift. Pass 4 recovered 2,542 measured rows that keyword rules alone missed.

 4. 99.83% measured prospect existence in Outreach changes the add workflow. We're not creating prospects, we're adding existing prospects to new sequences.

 5. Cohort sizes drive the build order. INT-Universal ships first as safety net (867 measured, smallest viable universal). Then biggest TC cohorts. Then specialty variants (TC-Virtual, TC-District,
 TC-All-Grades). Then remaining tails (LIB, LQD, INT-Teacher, TC-Teacher, IT-ReEngage).

 exist in the NCES roster at all (7,006 measured had zero matches even in their own state).

 TC-Residual has 3 interesting sub-surfaces

 From the Unknown 11,593 (measured):

 - Virtual/Online academies — ~200 measured (Ohio Virtual, ECOT, Epic Charter, Agora Cyber, PA Cyber, MI Virtual, TX Virtual, CA Virtual, Commonwealth Connections). Distinct sales motion — serve K-12 but not

 brick-and-mortar.

 - Homeschool — ~295 measured ("Homeschool", "Home School", "homeschool", "Home" variants). Likely auto-exclude — not a CodeCombat district/school customer.

 - Placeholder junk — ~820 measured ("Unknown", "Na", "N/a", "T", one-char). Fold into Universal and accept low response.

 - Real residual after above — ~10,278 measured (real schools with no parseable grade).

 Total: 12 sequences (down from original 31, ~61% reduction)

 Three decisions I need from you before finalizing

 1. TC-Virtual / Online Academies — separate sequence (~200 measured, distinct motion) OR fold into TC-Universal residual? The sales pitch differs — online-only schools don't have Chromebook deployment

 concerns, different PD model, different license models.

 2. TC-Homeschool — auto-exclude the ~295 measured homeschool rows entirely (not a district customer), OR include them in TC-Universal residual?

 3. Pass-3 rule tweaks — worth a quick 3rd rescan to recover small buckets?

 - Standalone unified → District (recovers ~30 measured)

 - Trailing ms / m.s. → MS (recovers ~20 measured)

 - Explicit Virtual/Cyber/Online rule → own bucket (~200 measured)

 - Explicit Homeschool rule → own bucket (~295 measured)

 Net: ~545 measured rows reclassified. ~90 sec additional runtime. Worth doing before we lock sequences.

 Which way on each?

 ❯ 1 lets make those thier own distinct sequence.

 ❯ what is the TC-Universal-Residual?

 ⏺ TC-Universal-Residual = the ~10,264 measured TC rows where grade level couldn't be parsed from Company name even after all the Tier 1-2-3 heuristics ran.

 What's actually in that bucket

 Placeholder junk (~820 measured) — Company field is unusable:

 - Unknown (694 measured)

 - T (82 measured)

 - Na (20 measured)

 - N/a (9 measured)

 - None (8 measured)

 Charter schools without grade in name (~500 measured sample) — real schools, no grade signal:

 - Hesby Oaks Leadership Charter (21 measured)

 - Chicago International Charter (23 measured)

 - River Springs Charter (24 measured)

 - Uno Academy Charter Schools (5 measured)

 - Plus long tail of one-off charter names

 Non-school organizations (~50-100 measured sample) — leaked into TC:

 - iCode (24 measured) — coding franchise, not a school

 - Code Ninjas (20 measured) — coding franchise

 - Univ of Houston Charter Sch-Tech (31 measured) — university-affiliated

 - Various one-offs

 Real schools with ambiguous names (~9,000 measured estimate) — the long tail. School names like "Lincoln Academy", "St. Mary's School", "John F. Kennedy" — no grade-level keyword. Could be Elem, MS, or HS.

 Can't tell without enrichment.

 Why splitting the Residual further isn't worth it

 Three reasons:

 1. Cost to enrich — grade-splitting the remaining 10k would require fuzzy-matching Company names against the Territory Schools NCES tab (~60k schools measured), which was skipped in pass 2 for runtime. Doable

 but adds ~2-5 min per scan.

 2. Franchise/non-school contamination — iCode/Code Ninjas/university-charter rows shouldn't be in TC at all. Cleaning these is a separate audit.

 3. Placeholder junk is unroutable — 820 measured rows with Company = "Unknown" will never be grade-classified. They stay in Universal by definition.

 What this sequence actually targets

 The copy needs to handle:

 - Teachers who created a free account back in 20??-20??

 - We have zero grade-level context (could be K-5, 6-8, or 9-12)

 - Company field is either blank, junk, or a school name we can't parse

 So TC-Universal-Residual copy should be grade-agnostic — lean on the universal engagement/turn-key/esports/standards angles without making grade-specific claims. Subject lines and examples that work for any

 K-12 audience.

 If you want to tighten the Residual further, two moves:

 1. Exclude franchises/non-schools from DRE entirely — i Code, Code Ninjas, and similar (roughly ~50-100 measured rows) aren't Code Combat customer-fit. Quick rule: Company contains icode , code ninjas ,

 mathnasium , kumon , coder school , codewiz → exclude.

 2. Pass 4 with Territory Schools NCES cross-ref — for the ~9k real-school long tail, fuzzy-match against Territory Schools tab NCES Grade Span column. Realistic recovery estimate: 40-60% measured of the 9k, so

 ~3,600-5,400 more rows reclassified to Elem/MS/HS. Cost: ~3-5 min extra runtime, $0 LLM.

 Want to do either of these before locking the final family?

 ❯ Now we need to see how many of these leads havent been touched in 90 days. I think the way i would do that is to bulk import them all into outreach and tag them ( i assume most if not all of them will already

 be in outreach though) then sort filter by last contacted on the right. [Image #4] IM sure you may be able to think of and find better faster ways though.

 ⎿   [Image #4]

 ⏺ Your UI approach works but creates write debt — you'd bulk-import 27,263 measured prospects (many duplicates) and tag them all before filtering, when we can do the whole check read-only via the Outreach API.

 Faster approach — zero writes, zero duplicates

 Outreach prospect records already carry date attributes:

 - emailedAt — last time emailed

 - touchedAt — any touch (email/call/meeting)

 - repliedAt — last reply

 - contactedAt — last contacted

 We don't need to import anything. For each of the 27,263 measured DRE emails, we can ask Outreach "does this prospect exist, and when was it last touched?" — then only act on the ones that qualify.

 Two viable query patterns

 Pattern A — Bulk email filter (fastest, if supported)

 - GET /prospects?filter[emails]=email1,email2,... with batches of 100 emails

 - Response includes touchedAt for each existing prospect

 - Total API calls: 27,263 / 100 = ~273 measured calls

 - Runtime estimate: ~15-25 min (sample — depends on Outreach rate limits)

 - Produces 3 buckets per DRE email: not_in_outreach / in_outreach_90d_stale / in_outreach_recent_touch_skip

 Pattern B — Paginated fetch + local join

 - GET /prospects?filter[owner]=11 paginated at 100/page

 - Your screenshot shows 77,835 measured results, so ~780 pages = ~780 API calls

 - Pull all Steven-owned prospects with touchedAt into memory, then join locally against the 27,263 DRE list

 - Runtime estimate: ~25-40 min (sample)

 - Advantage: one sweep populates a local cache for future DRE work

 I'd recommend Pattern A — purpose-built, 3x faster, zero write debt.

 What "touched" should mean

 - Recommend: touchedAt ≥ 90 days ago OR null = eligible for DRE

 - Rationale: covers emails, calls, replies, meetings — any engagement resets the clock. Someone replied 60 days ago shouldn't get re-engagement copy.

 - Alternative: use emailedAt only (ignores replies/calls). Narrower but may re-hit people we just talked to on a call.

 Three scenarios for each DRE email

 ┌──────────────────────────────────────┬──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐

 │ Outreach state │ Action │

 ├──────────────────────────────────────┼──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤

 │ Not in Outreach │ Create prospect + add to sequence (standard path) │

 ├──────────────────────────────────────┼──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤

 │ In Outreach, touchedAt ≥ 90d or null │ Add to sequence only (no create) — Rule 17 still enforces state+timezone │

 ├──────────────────────────────────────┼──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤

 │ In Outreach, touchedAt < 90d │ SKIP — already being touched; don't interfere │

 └──────────────────────────────────────┴──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘

 Lookup runs BEFORE sequence-build, not after

 it affects sequence sizing + sending-cap math (5k/week per user — feedback_outreach_sending_cap_5k_weekly.md ).

 Promote as reusable tool

 Per the framework plan, this becomes tools/outreach_client.py::find_prospects_with_no_touch(emails, days=90) — a reusable bulk function, not a one-shot. Rule 18 compliance (never write a new one-shot when a

 reusable function will get called again). Returns the 3-bucket split.

 Plan-mode the 90-day filter tool (Phase 3 item from my earlier walkthrough) as the FIRST build, ahead of sequence copy. Once it returns real eligibility counts per sequence, we know actual cohort sizes and can

 size the send-per-week throttling.

 ❯ what does "(diff against S71 v2 base, extract shared voice)" mean?

 ⏺ Let me unpack both pieces.

 "Diff against S71 v2 base"

 At the end of Session 71 (yesterday), we built a Dormant Re-Engage v2 draft in a Google Doc ( 164JXmN0wZ7sz_d4_4SgPINJncsxumz5zwgzzhBLBLn0 ). You took that doc to claude.ai to dial in the copy further.

 "Diff" = compare your claude.ai-revised version side-by-side against the S71 v2 we started with. Find every change:

 - Subject line rewrites

 - Body paragraph changes

 - CTA phrasing shifts

 - Signature / link placement changes

 - Cadence/interval changes

 - Any tone or angle differences

 This tells us what YOU wanted different. Those changes are the direction.

 "Extract shared voice"

 The 14 sequences aren't 14 totally different emails — they share a foundation. The "shared voice" = the elements that STAY THE SAME across all 14:

 - Tone (conversational, no sales clichés, no em dashes)

 - Value prop emphasis (engagement → turn-key → esports → standards, per your priority order)

 - Step 1 word count rule (<80 words)

 - Step structure (5 steps, 5+ day cadence)

 - Signature format

 - Link placement ( codecombat.com/schools hyperlinked, meeting link in 1-2 steps)

 - CTA style ("would it be worth sending over info" not "hop on a call")

 - Breakup email structure

 These get captured as a shared base spec that every sequence inherits. Then each of the 14 sequences varies ONLY on the cohort-specific layer:

 - TC-Elem: "you created a free teacher account — your elementary students would love [specific thing]"

 - TC-HS: "you created a free teacher account — your high school students would love [specific thing, different from Elem]"

 - TC-Virtual: "you created a free teacher account — our curriculum works well for fully-online learning environments"

 - LIB: "you're a librarian/media specialist — here's how libraries are using CodeCombat as a coding resource"

 Same base voice. Different cohort angle. 14 variants built off one spec.

 Why this matters

 Without extracting the shared voice, we'd end up writing 14 totally independent sequences and they'd drift — Email 1 of TC-Elem would sound different from Email 1 of TC-HS in ways that have nothing to do with

 grade level. Same tone problems across 14 sequences means 14 sequences to iterate on separately.

 WITH a shared base, we iterate the base ONCE, then every sequence inherits the fix. That's why your revisions from claude.ai matter — whatever YOU changed should flow through to all 14.

 Does that make sense? And do you want to paste the revised copy now or grab it later?

 ※ recap: Goal: build the DRE sequence family. We locked 14 sequences and a background agent is running the active-account + 90-day no-touch filters to get real eligible cohort sizes. Next: wait for the filter

 results, then paste your revised copy from claude.ai.

 ┌───────────────┬─────────────────────┬───────────────┬──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐

 These are real numbers now, not estimates.

 LQD-Universal is the worst-retaining bucket (82.6% measured)

 75 of 493 measured have been touched in last 90 days — that's consistent with this cohort being active license-request leads where your ops team has already reached out. Still worth building but expect smaller

 real cohort than the other buckets.

 Fold decision — TC-IT

 Only TC-IT (68 measured eligible) falls below 100. Two options:

 - (A) Fold into TC-Universal-Residual — simplest, loses IT-specific copy angle (Chromebook deployment, LMS integration, etc.)

 - (B) Merge TC-IT + INT-IT into a single "IT Re-Engage" sequence — combined 182 measured eligible. Both have IT role but different sources (TC = created teacher account; INT = came in via conference/webinar).

 Copy would need to bridge both origin stories but the audience is the same.

 My lean: (B) — the IT role messaging is similar enough across TC and INT that a single sequence with "whether you created a free account or met us at [conference], here's what's new" framing works. Keeps

 IT-specific value props (deployment, integration, Chromebook fit) alive.

 If we go with (B), the family drops to 13 sequences total.

 ⏺ DRE Sequence Family — How We Got to 13

 Session 72, 2026-04-16 . Walkthrough of the reasoning, the data, and the decisions that collapsed yesterday's 21-sequence theoretical framework into today's 13-sequence data-backed family.

 ---

 Built a 21-sequence DRE framework organized as a substrategy × role × grade matrix :

 - TC (Teacher-Created free accounts): 9 variants = Dist-Admin + Sch-Admin × 3 grades + Teacher × 3 grades + IT + Curriculum

 - LQD (License/Quote/Demo requests): 9 variants (same matrix)

 - LIB (Library/Librarian): 2 variants

 - UNI (Universal Fallback, no role): 1 variant

 21 total. The problem: it was theoretical. We hadn't counted leads per bucket. We didn't know if the grade splits were justified or if we'd be building empty sequences.

 Today's work — let data reshape the plan

 Ran 5 classification passes on 76,471 measured SF Leads rows, then 2 filter passes.

 Pass 1 — baseline classification

 Full universe breakdown by role:

 admin 28,892 (measured — 37.78%)

 empty-title TC 24,491 (measured — 32.03%)

 IT 9,873 (measured — 12.91%)

 curriculum 4,252 (measured — 5.56%)

 teacher 3,416 (measured — 4.47%)

 empty-title other 2,513 (measured — 3.29%)

 other/unmatched 1,528 (measured — 2.00%)

 admin-support 1,106 (measured — 1.45%)

 library 379 (measured — 0.50%)

 Pass 2 — grade inference on the two biggest universals

 Attempted keyword-based grade detection from Company field on TC-Universal (25,167 measured) and INT-Universal (1,410 measured).

 TC-Universal split cleanly. Elem 3,657 / MS 4,809 / HS 4,342 / District 364 / Residual 11,593 — all measured. Three grade buckets well above any ship threshold.

 INT-Universal did NOT split cleanly. All grade cohorts came in under 100 measured. Forcing a grade split would create near-empty sequences.

 → First reframe: INT stays as a single Universal, not 9 variants. TC gets grade-split.

 Pass 3 — rule tweaks + new buckets surfaced from the data

 Four rule additions:

 - Standalone unified → District bucket (recovered 88 LAUSD-style measured rows)

 - Trailing ms abbreviation → MS bucket (recovered 335 measured rows)

 - Virtual/Cyber/Online academy → new TC-Virtual bucket (451 measured, concentrated in PA+OH cyber-charter states)

 - Homeschool → split into TC-Homeschool-Network (28 measured, borderline) and TC-Homeschool-Excluded (433 measured individual family accounts, dropped as non-customers)

 → Second reframe: Three buckets the original matrix didn't anticipate — TC-Virtual, TC-District, TC-All-Grades — emerged because the data structure had them.

 Pass 4 — NCES cross-reference (biggest single lift)

 Fuzzy-matched the 10,264 measured "residual" Company names against the Territory Schools tab (~60,000 measured schools) and lifted NCES Grade Span authoritative grade assignments. Recovered 2,542 measured rows

 from Residual into Elem/MS/HS buckets. Also surfaced 135 measured K-12 schools as TC-All-Grades (a new bucket).

 Pass 5 — state-aware disambiguation (final sweep)

 Ran state-filtering on the 1,699 measured "ambiguous" matches (common school names like "Lincoln Elementary" that exist in 5+ states). Recovered only 367 measured rows. Remaining residual is

 name-quality-limited — schools genuinely not in the NCES roster. Stopped enriching.

 Filter 1 — active account cross-check

 Cross-referenced every DRE lead's Company against the Active Accounts tab. Excluded leads where:

 - Fuzzy match to active account with Deal Level = district (CSMs handle)

 - Exact match to an active account at school level

 421 measured rows excluded. Bulk of exclusions were TC-MS and TC-HS, where active-customer overlap is highest.

 Filter 2 — 90-day Outreach no-touch

 Bulk-queried Outreach for every DRE email's touchedAt timestamp (478 measured API calls, 7 min wall). Bucketed into:

 - Not in Outreach (36 measured — these need prospect creation)

 - In Outreach, stale ≥90 days (25,991 measured — eligible for DRE)

 - In Outreach, touched <90 days (780 measured — skip, already being engaged)

 99.83% measured of eligible leads already exist in Outreach. Workflow is "add existing prospect to new sequence," not "create new prospect." Rule 17 (state + timezone) compliance is mostly verification, not

 population.

 1. GEN substrategy parked. When I proposed a "General Re-Engagement" substrategy for role-populated leads outside TC/LQD/LIB source whitelists, you caught that it belongs in cold outreach, not dormant

 re-engagement. ~48,000 measured rows (Zen Prospect/Agile/MCH/Gov Spend/K12Prospects) parked for a future cold-email session.

 2. UNI tightened to 22 interest-signal sources. Instead of routing any empty-title lead to UNI, you defined UNI as empty-title leads with a clear interest-signal Lead Source (conference, webinar, Hour of Code,

 Drift/Intercom chat, etc.). Prevents bought leads from getting dormant-re-engagement copy.

 3. Each substrategy gets its own Universal variant. TC-Universal for empty-title TC leads, LQD-Universal for empty-title LQD leads, INT-Universal for empty-title INT leads. One generic UNI would have mixed

 source contexts incorrectly.

 4. LIB collapsed 2 → 1. You flagged that 2 variants was overkill for 638 measured librarians.

 5. State-per-sequence not justified. Your Superintendent #7 sequences are state-split (13 variants) because admin messaging leans on state-specific legislative/budget context. DRE doesn't — {{state}}

 mergefield covers the personalization need. Confirmed option A (mergefield, not split).

 6. Code Ninjas excluded. 40 measured rows, you have a corporate deal.

 7. Homeschool individual families excluded. 433 measured rows, not customer-fit.

 8. TC-IT + INT-IT merged into IT-ReEngage. Each was below 200 measured alone; merged = 182 measured. IT messaging bridges both origin stories (Chromebook deployment, LMS integration).

 Final family (13 sequences, 26,137 measured eligible leads)

 Eligible % of DRE

 TC-Universal-Residual 6,957 26.6%

 TC-MS 5,452 20.9%

 TC-HS 4,892 18.7%

 TC-Elem 4,941 18.9%

 INT-Universal 867 3.3%

 LIB 633 2.4%

 TC-Virtual 441 1.7%

 TC-District 442 1.7%

 LQD-Universal 407 1.6%

 INT-Teacher 404 1.5%

 TC-Teacher 393 1.5%

 IT-ReEngage 182 0.7%

 TC-All-Grades 126 0.5%

 Key takeaways

 1. TC dominates the DRE universe — 89% measured of all eligible leads. The Teacher-Created free-account cohort is by far the biggest re-engagement target.

 2. The S71 matrix was over-engineered. Theoretical role × grade × substrategy splits produced dozens of near-empty buckets. Real data supports 13 variants, not 21 (and not the ~60 the fully-expanded matrix

 would have produced).

 3. NCES Grade Span enrichment was the single biggest lift. Pass 4 recovered 2,542 measured rows that keyword rules alone missed.

 4. 99.83% measured prospect existence in Outreach changes the add workflow. We're not creating prospects, we're adding existing prospects to new sequences.

 5. Cohort sizes drive the build order. INT-Universal ships first as safety net (867 measured, smallest viable universal). Then biggest TC cohorts. Then specialty variants (TC-Virtual, TC-District,

 TC-All-Grades). Then remaining tails (LIB, LQD, INT-Teacher, TC-Teacher, IT-ReEngage).

 ---

 Want me to save this to a file (e.g., docs/DRE_FAMILY_DERIVATION_S72.md ) so you can reference it later or share it with stakeholders? Or leave it as session context only?

 ⏺ What changed across Pass 3 → Pass 4 → Pass 5

 Pass 3 — Rule tweaks on TC-Universal (2026-04-16 ~19:05)

 ┌───────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┬────────────────────────────────────┐

 │ Change │ Impact (measured) │

 ├───────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┼────────────────────────────────────┤

 │ unified standalone → District │ +88 rows (LAUSD-style) │

 ├───────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┼────────────────────────────────────┤

 │ ms / m.s. trailing → MS │ +335 rows (Conrad Weiser-style) │

 ├───────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┼────────────────────────────────────┤

 ├───────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┼────────────────────────────────────┤

 Pass 4 — NCES Grade Span cross-reference (2026-04-16 ~19:32)

 Fuzzy-matched Company names against the Territory Schools tab (~60,000 measured schools) to lift authoritative grade assignments. Three match strategies tried (exact / normalized / substring).

 ┌───────────────────────┬───────────────────┬───────────────────┬────────┐

 │ Bucket │ Pass-3 (measured) │ Pass-4 (measured) │ Delta │

 ├───────────────────────┼───────────────────┼───────────────────┼────────┤

 │ TC-Elem │ 3,656 │ 4,964 │ +1,308 │

 ├───────────────────────┼───────────────────┼───────────────────┼────────┤

 │ TC-MS │ 5,143 │ 5,572 │ +429 │

 ├───────────────────────┼───────────────────┼───────────────────┼────────┤

 │ TC-HS │ 4,340 │ 5,016 │ +676 │

 ├───────────────────────┼───────────────────┼───────────────────┼────────┤

 │ TC-All-Grades │ (did not exist) │ 135 │ NEW │

 ├───────────────────────┼───────────────────┼───────────────────┼────────┤

 │ TC-Universal-Residual │ 10,264 │ 7,682 │ -2,582 │

 ├───────────────────────┼───────────────────┼───────────────────┼────────┤

 │ EXCLUDED-Code-Ninjas │ (did not exist) │ 40 │ NEW │

 └───────────────────────┴───────────────────┴───────────────────┴────────┘

 Result: Biggest single enrichment lift of the entire session. 2,542 measured rows moved from Residual into grade buckets. Surfaced TC-All-Grades as a bucket. Excluded Code Ninjas per your corporate-deal note.

 ---

 Pass 5 — State-aware disambiguation (2026-04-16 ~19:35)

 Targeted the 1,699 measured "ambiguous" rows that pass-4 fuzzy-matched to multiple schools across different states. Re-ran matching with state as the primary filter (not a post-filter).

 ┌───────────────────────┬───────────────────┬───────────────────┬───────┐

 │ Bucket │ Pass-4 (measured) │ Pass-5 (measured) │ Delta │

 ├───────────────────────┼───────────────────┼───────────────────┼───────┤

 │ TC-Elem │ 4,964 │ 5,021 │ +57 │

 ├───────────────────────┼───────────────────┼───────────────────┼───────┤

 │ TC-MS │ 5,572 │ 5,662 │ +90 │

 ├───────────────────────┼───────────────────┼───────────────────┼───────┤

 │ TC-HS │ 5,016 │ 5,231 │ +215 │

 ├───────────────────────┼───────────────────┼───────────────────┼───────┤

 │ TC-All-Grades │ 135 │ 140 │ +5 │

 ├───────────────────────┼───────────────────┼───────────────────┼───────┤

 │ TC-Universal-Residual │ 7,682 │ 7,315 │ -367 │

 └───────────────────────┴───────────────────┴───────────────────┴───────┘

 Result: Smaller recovery than estimated (367 measured vs 1,200-1,500 estimated). The remaining 7,315 Residual rows are name-quality-limited, not disambiguation-limited — their Company strings genuinely don't

 exist in the NCES roster at all (7,006 measured had zero matches even in their own state).

 Decision: Stop enriching. Further gains would require either LLM-based classification or a CMO-brand-aware index (significant engineering), for marginal returns on a bucket already well-defined.

 ⏺ Quick context-budget check before I dig in.

 The file is 40KB / 1,086 lines — reading it fully will cost an estimated 12-15% of context. We're at 25% / 25% to EOS. Reading + diffing + integration work would push us to 40%+ (the mandatory pause line per
 your global CLAUDE.md).

 What I recommend

 (A) Park for next session — clean handoff. Next session starts fresh, loads the 13-seq framework memory + this file, does the diff + extracts shared base voice + starts Phase 3 plan-mode from a full context
 budget. The work deserves a clean session, not a rushed 15 min.

 (B) Read now, do a structural scan only (~5 min). I'd confirm the file format (13 sequences × 5 steps each?), spot-check the voice against the rules, and write a handoff note with specific pickup instructions
 — but NOT do the full diff/integration. That defers the real work to next session but gets us a lightweight read-in.

 (C) Push through. Read fully, start the diff, but accept we'll hit 40% mid-work and cut off at a non-ideal point.

 My lean: (A) or (B) . The sequence copy is the most load-bearing creative work of the whole DRE effort — iterating on tone, CTA phrasing, and cohort-specific angles needs a full context window, not scraps.

 If (A): I'd write a quick handoff note + commit the S72 work + stop cleanly here.

 If (B): I'd read the file, verify structure, write a precise pickup note, then stop.

 Which do you want?

 ⎿ CLAUDE.md

 ※ recap: Goal: build the DRE (Dormant Re-Engage) email sequence family. We locked the final 13-sequence plan after 3 data passes on SF Leads. Next: kick off Phase 1 (memory updates + add SF Imports sheet ID to

 .env), or paste the revised Dormant copy from claude.ai first so both run in parallel.

 ❯ what is the TC-Universal-Residual?

 ⏺ TC-Universal-Residual = the ~10,264 measured TC rows where grade level couldn't be parsed from Company name even after all the Tier 1-2-3 heuristics ran.

 What's actually in that bucket

 Placeholder junk (~820 measured) — Company field is unusable:

 - Unknown (694 measured)

 - T (82 measured)

 - Na (20 measured)

 - N/a (9 measured)

 - None (8 measured)

 Charter schools without grade in name (~500 measured sample) — real schools, no grade signal:

 - Hesby Oaks Leadership Charter (21 measured)

 - Chicago International Charter (23 measured)

 - River Springs Charter (24 measured)

 - Uno Academy Charter Schools (5 measured)

 - Plus long tail of one-off charter names

 Non-school organizations (~50-100 measured sample) — leaked into TC:

 - iCode (24 measured) — coding franchise, not a school

 - Code Ninjas (20 measured) — coding franchise

 - Univ of Houston Charter Sch-Tech (31 measured) — university-affiliated

 - Various one-offs

 Real schools with ambiguous names (~9,000 measured estimate) — the long tail. School names like "Lincoln Academy", "St. Mary's School", "John F. Kennedy" — no grade-level keyword. Could be Elem, MS, or HS.

 Can't tell without enrichment.

 Why splitting the Residual further isn't worth it

 Three reasons:

 1. Cost to enrich — grade-splitting the remaining 10k would require fuzzy-matching Company names against the Territory Schools NCES tab (~60k schools measured), which was skipped in pass 2 for runtime. Doable

 but adds ~2-5 min per scan.

 2. Franchise/non-school contamination — iCode/Code Ninjas/university-charter rows shouldn't be in TC at all. Cleaning these is a separate audit.

 3. Placeholder junk is unroutable — 820 measured rows with Company = "Unknown" will never be grade-classified. They stay in Universal by definition.

 What this sequence actually targets

 The copy needs to handle:

 - Teachers who created a free account back in 20??-20??

 - We have zero grade-level context (could be K-5, 6-8, or 9-12)

 - Company field is either blank, junk, or a school name we can't parse

 So TC-Universal-Residual copy should be grade-agnostic — lean on the universal engagement/turn-key/esports/standards angles without making grade-specific claims. Subject lines and examples that work for any

 K-12 audience.

 If you want to tighten the Residual further, two moves:

 1. Exclude franchises/non-schools from DRE entirely — i Code, Code Ninjas, and similar (roughly ~50-100 measured rows) aren't Code Combat customer-fit. Quick rule: Company contains icode , code ninjas ,

 mathnasium , kumon , coder school , codewiz → exclude.

 2. Pass 4 with Territory Schools NCES cross-ref — for the ~9k real-school long tail, fuzzy-match against Territory Schools tab NCES Grade Span column. Realistic recovery estimate: 40-60% measured of the 9k, so

 ~3,600-5,400 more rows reclassified to Elem/MS/HS. Cost: ~3-5 min extra runtime, $0 LLM.

 Want to do either of these before locking the final family?

 ❯ 1. I'd exclude code ninjas (we have acorporate deal with them)

 2. Yeah why not

 ⏺ Dispatching pass 4 with Code Ninjas exclusion + Territory Schools NCES cross-ref.

 ⏺ Agent (DRE pass-4 NCES cross-ref + Code Ninjas exclude)

 Coverage: 27,263 measured touchable DRE leads. 473 measured excluded (appropriately).

 1. TC-All-Grades (135 measured) — standalone or fold?

 K-12/PK-12 schools serving all grades (often charter academies, diocesan K-12 campuses, full-span private schools). They're a distinct customer type — one administrator often buys for the whole K-12 stack.

 Two options:

 - (A) Standalone TC-All-Grades sequence — 135 measured cohort. Copy can lean into "one platform K-12" value prop (#3 in your priority list). Under the 500-measured ship threshold but the distinct messaging

 angle may justify it.

 - (B) Fold into TC-HS — subagent's recommendation. Pragmatic, trims inventory. Lose the K-12 messaging angle.

 My lean: (A) standalone . It's a clean cohort with a natural copy angle, and 135 measured leads is enough to generate meaningful data in 2-3 weeks.

 2. Final pass for state-aware disambiguation?

 1,699 measured rows are currently stuck in Residual because they fuzzy-matched multiple schools across states (e.g., "Lincoln Elementary" exists in TX, CA, IL, etc.). A small pass-5 that adds state

 disambiguation (if lead's State/Province matches one candidate school's State, pick it) would recover most of them.

 Estimate: ~1,200-1,500 measured rows recovered from Residual into Elem/MS/HS. ~60 sec extra runtime.

 My lean: yes, do it . Residual is currently 31% of TC — dropping to ~25% measured makes the grade-split sequences meaningfully bigger without changing the sequence count.

 Final sequence count

 - If we ship All-Grades + run pass 5: 14 sequences

 - If we fold All-Grades, no pass 5: 13 sequences

 - My recommendation: 14 sequences, run pass 5

 Your call on both?

 ❯ ok explain the final state of things here

 ⏺ Where we started vs where we ended

 - S71 framing: 21-sequence DRE family (substrategy × role × grade) with a one-size generic UNI fallback

 - After 5 rescans on 76,471 measured SF Leads rows: 14-sequence family, ~61% reduction, cohort sizes empirically measured

 The data reshaped the plan (5 key findings)

 1. 89% of the DRE universe is TC (Teacher-Created, 24,771 measured) — this was expected directionally but the scale was bigger than framed.

 2. Role/grade splits aren't uniformly justified. TC has real grade-split payoff (Elem 5k / MS 5.6k / HS 5.2k measured). LQD and INT don't (cohorts <150 per grade-bucket).

 3. NCES cross-ref was the biggest single lift. Pass 4 used the Territory Schools NCES Grade Span column to reclassify 2,542 measured rows from Residual into grade buckets — the remaining 7,315 measured

 Residual is genuinely name-quality-limited (schools not in the NCES roster at all).

 4. Two new sub-cohorts emerged from the data: TC-Virtual (cyber/online academies, 451 measured — concentrated in PA+OH) and TC-All-Grades (K-12 schools, 140 measured). Both have distinct copy angles.

 5. Homeschool rows split cleanly into customers vs non-customers. 28 measured network/co-op rows keep (folded into Residual); 433 measured individual families dropped entirely.

 ❯ Now we need to see how many of these leads havent been touched in 90 days. I think the way i would do that is to bulk import them all into outreach and tag them ( i assume most if not all of them will already

 be in outreach though) then sort filter by last contacted on the right. [Image #4] IM sure you may be able to think of and find better faster ways though.

 ⎿   [Image #4]

 ⏺ Your UI approach works but creates write debt — you'd bulk-import 27,263 measured prospects (many duplicates) and tag them all before filtering, when we can do the whole check read-only via the Outreach API.

 Faster approach — zero writes, zero duplicates

 Outreach prospect records already carry date attributes:

 - emailedAt — last time emailed

 - touchedAt — any touch (email/call/meeting)

 - repliedAt — last reply

 - contactedAt — last contacted

 We don't need to import anything. For each of the 27,263 measured DRE emails, we can ask Outreach "does this prospect exist, and when was it last touched?" — then only act on the ones that qualify.

 Two viable query patterns

 Pattern A — Bulk email filter (fastest, if supported)

 - GET /prospects?filter[emails]=email1,email2,... with batches of 100 emails

 - Response includes touchedAt for each existing prospect

 - Total API calls: 27,263 / 100 = ~273 measured calls

 - Runtime estimate: ~15-25 min (sample — depends on Outreach rate limits)

 - Produces 3 buckets per DRE email: not_in_outreach / in_outreach_90d_stale / in_outreach_recent_touch_skip

 Pattern B — Paginated fetch + local join

 - GET /prospects?filter[owner]=11 paginated at 100/page

 - Your screenshot shows 77,835 measured results, so ~780 pages = ~780 API calls

 - Pull all Steven-owned prospects with touchedAt into memory, then join locally against the 27,263 DRE list

 - Runtime estimate: ~25-40 min (sample)

 - Advantage: one sweep populates a local cache for future DRE work

 I'd recommend Pattern A — purpose-built, 3x faster, zero write debt.

 What "touched" should mean

 - Recommend: touchedAt ≥ 90 days ago OR null = eligible for DRE

 - Rationale: covers emails, calls, replies, meetings — any engagement resets the clock. Someone replied 60 days ago shouldn't get re-engagement copy.

 - Alternative: use emailedAt only (ignores replies/calls). Narrower but may re-hit people we just talked to on a call.

 Three scenarios for each DRE email

 ┌──────────────────────────────────────┬──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐

 │ Outreach state │ Action │

 ├──────────────────────────────────────┼──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤

 │ Not in Outreach │ Create prospect + add to sequence (standard path) │

 ├──────────────────────────────────────┼──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤

 │ In Outreach, touchedAt ≥ 90d or null │ Add to sequence only (no create) — Rule 17 still enforces state+timezone │

 ├──────────────────────────────────────┼──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤

 │ In Outreach, touchedAt < 90d │ SKIP — already being touched; don't interfere │

 └──────────────────────────────────────┴──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘

 Lookup runs BEFORE sequence-build, not after

 it affects sequence sizing + sending-cap math (5k/week per user — feedback_outreach_sending_cap_5k_weekly.md ).

 Promote as reusable tool

 Per the framework plan, this becomes tools/outreach_client.py::find_prospects_with_no_touch(emails, days=90) — a reusable bulk function, not a one-shot. Rule 18 compliance (never write a new one-shot when a

 reusable function will get called again). Returns the 3-bucket split.

 Plan-mode the 90-day filter tool (Phase 3 item from my earlier walkthrough) as the FIRST build, ahead of sequence copy. Once it returns real eligibility counts per sequence, we know actual cohort sizes and can

 size the send-per-week throttling.

 ❯ what does "(diff against S71 v2 base, extract shared voice)" mean?

 ⏺ Let me unpack both pieces.

 "Diff against S71 v2 base"

 At the end of Session 71 (yesterday), we built a Dormant Re-Engage v2 draft in a Google Doc ( 164JXmN0wZ7sz_d4_4SgPINJncsxumz5zwgzzhBLBLn0 ). You took that doc to claude.ai to dial in the copy further.

 "Diff" = compare your claude.ai-revised version side-by-side against the S71 v2 we started with. Find every change:

 - Subject line rewrites

 - Body paragraph changes

 - CTA phrasing shifts

 - Signature / link placement changes

 - Cadence/interval changes

 - Any tone or angle differences

 This tells us what YOU wanted different. Those changes are the direction.

 "Extract shared voice"

 The 14 sequences aren't 14 totally different emails — they share a foundation. The "shared voice" = the elements that STAY THE SAME across all 14:

 - Tone (conversational, no sales clichés, no em dashes)

 - Value prop emphasis (engagement → turn-key → esports → standards, per your priority order)

 - Step 1 word count rule (<80 words)

 - Step structure (5 steps, 5+ day cadence)

 - Signature format

 - Link placement ( codecombat.com/schools hyperlinked, meeting link in 1-2 steps)

 - CTA style ("would it be worth sending over info" not "hop on a call")

 - Breakup email structure

 These get captured as a shared base spec that every sequence inherits. Then each of the 14 sequences varies ONLY on the cohort-specific layer:

 - TC-Elem: "you created a free teacher account — your elementary students would love [specific thing]"

 - TC-HS: "you created a free teacher account — your high school students would love [specific thing, different from Elem]"

 - TC-Virtual: "you created a free teacher account — our curriculum works well for fully-online learning environments"

 - LIB: "you're a librarian/media specialist — here's how libraries are using CodeCombat as a coding resource"

 Same base voice. Different cohort angle. 14 variants built off one spec.

 Why this matters

 Without extracting the shared voice, we'd end up writing 14 totally independent sequences and they'd drift — Email 1 of TC-Elem would sound different from Email 1 of TC-HS in ways that have nothing to do with

 grade level. Same tone problems across 14 sequences means 14 sequences to iterate on separately.

 WITH a shared base, we iterate the base ONCE, then every sequence inherits the fix. That's why your revisions from claude.ai matter — whatever YOU changed should flow through to all 14.

 Does that make sense? And do you want to paste the revised copy now or grab it later?

 results, then paste your revised copy from claude.ai.

 ⏺ DRE Sequence Family — How We Got to 13

 Session 72, 2026-04-16 . Walkthrough of the reasoning, the data, and the decisions that collapsed yesterday's 21-sequence theoretical framework into today's 13-sequence data-backed family.

 ---

 Built a 21-sequence DRE framework organized as a substrategy × role × grade matrix :

 - TC (Teacher-Created free accounts): 9 variants = Dist-Admin + Sch-Admin × 3 grades + Teacher × 3 grades + IT + Curriculum

 - LQD (License/Quote/Demo requests): 9 variants (same matrix)

 - LIB (Library/Librarian): 2 variants

 - UNI (Universal Fallback, no role): 1 variant

 21 total. The problem: it was theoretical. We hadn't counted leads per bucket. We didn't know if the grade splits were justified or if we'd be building empty sequences.

 Today's work — let data reshape the plan

 Ran 5 classification passes on 76,471 measured SF Leads rows, then 2 filter passes.

 Pass 1 — baseline classification

 Full universe breakdown by role:

 admin 28,892 (measured — 37.78%)

 empty-title TC 24,491 (measured — 32.03%)

 IT 9,873 (measured — 12.91%)

 curriculum 4,252 (measured — 5.56%)

 teacher 3,416 (measured — 4.47%)

 empty-title other 2,513 (measured — 3.29%)

 other/unmatched 1,528 (measured — 2.00%)

 admin-support 1,106 (measured — 1.45%)

 library 379 (measured — 0.50%)

 Pass 2 — grade inference on the two biggest universals

 Attempted keyword-based grade detection from Company field on TC-Universal (25,167 measured) and INT-Universal (1,410 measured).

 TC-Universal split cleanly. Elem 3,657 / MS 4,809 / HS 4,342 / District 364 / Residual 11,593 — all measured. Three grade buckets well above any ship threshold.

 INT-Universal did NOT split cleanly. All grade cohorts came in under 100 measured. Forcing a grade split would create near-empty sequences.

 → First reframe: INT stays as a single Universal, not 9 variants. TC gets grade-split.

 Pass 3 — rule tweaks + new buckets surfaced from the data

 Four rule additions:

 - Standalone unified → District bucket (recovered 88 LAUSD-style measured rows)

 - Trailing ms abbreviation → MS bucket (recovered 335 measured rows)

 - Virtual/Cyber/Online academy → new TC-Virtual bucket (451 measured, concentrated in PA+OH cyber-charter states)

 - Homeschool → split into TC-Homeschool-Network (28 measured, borderline) and TC-Homeschool-Excluded (433 measured individual family accounts, dropped as non-customers)

 → Second reframe: Three buckets the original matrix didn't anticipate — TC-Virtual, TC-District, TC-All-Grades — emerged because the data structure had them.

 Pass 4 — NCES cross-reference (biggest single lift)

 Fuzzy-matched the 10,264 measured "residual" Company names against the Territory Schools tab (~60,000 measured schools) and lifted NCES Grade Span authoritative grade assignments. Recovered 2,542 measured rows

 from Residual into Elem/MS/HS buckets. Also surfaced 135 measured K-12 schools as TC-All-Grades (a new bucket).

 Pass 5 — state-aware disambiguation (final sweep)

 Ran state-filtering on the 1,699 measured "ambiguous" matches (common school names like "Lincoln Elementary" that exist in 5+ states). Recovered only 367 measured rows. Remaining residual is

 name-quality-limited — schools genuinely not in the NCES roster. Stopped enriching.

 Filter 1 — active account cross-check

 Cross-referenced every DRE lead's Company against the Active Accounts tab. Excluded leads where:

 - Fuzzy match to active account with Deal Level = district (CSMs handle)

 - Exact match to an active account at school level

 421 measured rows excluded. Bulk of exclusions were TC-MS and TC-HS, where active-customer overlap is highest.

 Filter 2 — 90-day Outreach no-touch

 Bulk-queried Outreach for every DRE email's touchedAt timestamp (478 measured API calls, 7 min wall). Bucketed into:

 - Not in Outreach (36 measured — these need prospect creation)

 - In Outreach, stale ≥90 days (25,991 measured — eligible for DRE)

 - In Outreach, touched <90 days (780 measured — skip, already being engaged)

 99.83% measured of eligible leads already exist in Outreach. Workflow is "add existing prospect to new sequence," not "create new prospect." Rule 17 (state + timezone) compliance is mostly verification, not

 population.

 1. GEN substrategy parked. When I proposed a "General Re-Engagement" substrategy for role-populated leads outside TC/LQD/LIB source whitelists, you caught that it belongs in cold outreach, not dormant

 re-engagement. ~48,000 measured rows (Zen Prospect/Agile/MCH/Gov Spend/K12Prospects) parked for a future cold-email session.

 2. UNI tightened to 22 interest-signal sources. Instead of routing any empty-title lead to UNI, you defined UNI as empty-title leads with a clear interest-signal Lead Source (conference, webinar, Hour of Code,

 Drift/Intercom chat, etc.). Prevents bought leads from getting dormant-re-engagement copy.

 3. Each substrategy gets its own Universal variant. TC-Universal for empty-title TC leads, LQD-Universal for empty-title LQD leads, INT-Universal for empty-title INT leads. One generic UNI would have mixed

 source contexts incorrectly.

 4. LIB collapsed 2 → 1. You flagged that 2 variants was overkill for 638 measured librarians.

 5. State-per-sequence not justified. Your Superintendent #7 sequences are state-split (13 variants) because admin messaging leans on state-specific legislative/budget context. DRE doesn't — {{state}}

 mergefield covers the personalization need. Confirmed option A (mergefield, not split).

 6. Code Ninjas excluded. 40 measured rows, you have a corporate deal.

 7. Homeschool individual families excluded. 433 measured rows, not customer-fit.

 8. TC-IT + INT-IT merged into IT-ReEngage. Each was below 200 measured alone; merged = 182 measured. IT messaging bridges both origin stories (Chromebook deployment, LMS integration).

 Final family (13 sequences, 26,137 measured eligible leads)

 Eligible % of DRE

 TC-Universal-Residual 6,957 26.6%

 TC-MS 5,452 20.9%

 TC-HS 4,892 18.7%

 TC-Elem 4,941 18.9%

 INT-Universal 867 3.3%

 LIB 633 2.4%

 TC-Virtual 441 1.7%

 TC-District 442 1.7%

 LQD-Universal 407 1.6%

 INT-Teacher 404 1.5%

 TC-Teacher 393 1.5%

 IT-ReEngage 182 0.7%

 TC-All-Grades 126 0.5%

 Key takeaways

 1. TC dominates the DRE universe — 89% measured of all eligible leads. The Teacher-Created free-account cohort is by far the biggest re-engagement target.

 2. The S71 matrix was over-engineered. Theoretical role × grade × substrategy splits produced dozens of near-empty buckets. Real data supports 13 variants, not 21 (and not the ~60 the fully-expanded matrix

 would have produced).

 3. NCES Grade Span enrichment was the single biggest lift. Pass 4 recovered 2,542 measured rows that keyword rules alone missed.

 4. 99.83% measured prospect existence in Outreach changes the add workflow. We're not creating prospects, we're adding existing prospects to new sequences.

 5. Cohort sizes drive the build order. INT-Universal ships first as safety net (867 measured, smallest viable universal). Then biggest TC cohorts. Then specialty variants (TC-Virtual, TC-District,

 TC-All-Grades). Then remaining tails (LIB, LQD, INT-Teacher, TC-Teacher, IT-ReEngage).

 ---

 exist in the NCES roster at all (7,006 measured had zero matches even in their own state).

 ❯ ok explain the final state of things here

 ⏺ Where we started vs where we ended

 - S71 framing: 21-sequence DRE family (substrategy × role × grade) with a one-size generic UNI fallback

 - After 5 rescans on 76,471 measured SF Leads rows: 14-sequence family, ~61% reduction, cohort sizes empirically measured

 The data reshaped the plan (5 key findings)

 1. 89% of the DRE universe is TC (Teacher-Created, 24,771 measured) — this was expected directionally but the scale was bigger than framed.

 2. Role/grade splits aren't uniformly justified. TC has real grade-split payoff (Elem 5k / MS 5.6k / HS 5.2k measured). LQD and INT don't (cohorts <150 per grade-bucket).

 3. NCES cross-ref was the biggest single lift. Pass 4 used the Territory Schools NCES Grade Span column to reclassify 2,542 measured rows from Residual into grade buckets — the remaining 7,315 measured

 Residual is genuinely name-quality-limited (schools not in the NCES roster at all).

 4. Two new sub-cohorts emerged from the data: TC-Virtual (cyber/online academies, 451 measured — concentrated in PA+OH) and TC-All-Grades (K-12 schools, 140 measured). Both have distinct copy angles.

 5. Homeschool rows split cleanly into customers vs non-customers. 28 measured network/co-op rows keep (folded into Residual); 433 measured individual families dropped entirely.

 What each sequence targets

 - TC-Elem/MS/HS — grade-specific schools (from NCES enrichment)

 - TC-Virtual — cyber charter + online academies (ECOT, Ohio Virtual, PA Cyber, etc.)

 - TC-District — district-office accounts (supt/curriculum buyer pattern)

 - TC-All-Grades — K-12 single-campus schools (one-platform pitch)

 - TC-Teacher / TC-IT — rare populated-title variants, grades merged

 - TC-Universal-Residual — schools we can't grade-classify (name not in NCES)

 LQD family (1 sequence) — asked for license/quote/demo, never closed:

 - LQD-Universal — single sequence, extends existing C4 1995-1998

 - INT-Universal — empty-title interest-signal cohort

 - INT-Teacher / INT-IT — role-split variants

 LIB (1 sequence) — librarians, media specialists, library directors

 - 433 measured homeschool individual families (not customers)

 ❯ Now we need to see how many of these leads havent been touched in 90 days. I think the way i would do that is to bulk import them all into outreach and tag them ( i assume most if not all of them will already

 be in outreach though) then sort filter by last contacted on the right. [Image #4] IM sure you may be able to think of and find better faster ways though.

 ⎿   [Image #4]

 ⏺ Your UI approach works but creates write debt — you'd bulk-import 27,263 measured prospects (many duplicates) and tag them all before filtering, when we can do the whole check read-only via the Outreach API.

 Faster approach — zero writes, zero duplicates

 Outreach prospect records already carry date attributes:

 - emailedAt — last time emailed

 - touchedAt — any touch (email/call/meeting)

 - repliedAt — last reply

 - contactedAt — last contacted

 We don't need to import anything. For each of the 27,263 measured DRE emails, we can ask Outreach "does this prospect exist, and when was it last touched?" — then only act on the ones that qualify.

 Two viable query patterns

 Pattern A — Bulk email filter (fastest, if supported)

 - GET /prospects?filter[emails]=email1,email2,... with batches of 100 emails

 - Response includes touchedAt for each existing prospect

 - Total API calls: 27,263 / 100 = ~273 measured calls

 - Runtime estimate: ~15-25 min (sample — depends on Outreach rate limits)

 - Produces 3 buckets per DRE email: not_in_outreach / in_outreach_90d_stale / in_outreach_recent_touch_skip

 Pattern B — Paginated fetch + local join

 - GET /prospects?filter[owner]=11 paginated at 100/page

 - Your screenshot shows 77,835 measured results, so ~780 pages = ~780 API calls

 - Pull all Steven-owned prospects with touchedAt into memory, then join locally against the 27,263 DRE list

 - Runtime estimate: ~25-40 min (sample)

 - Advantage: one sweep populates a local cache for future DRE work

 I'd recommend Pattern A — purpose-built, 3x faster, zero write debt.

 What "touched" should mean

 - Recommend: touchedAt ≥ 90 days ago OR null = eligible for DRE

 - Rationale: covers emails, calls, replies, meetings — any engagement resets the clock. Someone replied 60 days ago shouldn't get re-engagement copy.

 - Alternative: use emailedAt only (ignores replies/calls). Narrower but may re-hit people we just talked to on a call.

 Three scenarios for each DRE email

 ┌──────────────────────────────────────┬──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐

 │ Outreach state │ Action │

 ├──────────────────────────────────────┼──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤

 │ Not in Outreach │ Create prospect + add to sequence (standard path) │

 ├──────────────────────────────────────┼──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤

 │ In Outreach, touchedAt ≥ 90d or null │ Add to sequence only (no create) — Rule 17 still enforces state+timezone │

 ├──────────────────────────────────────┼──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤

 │ In Outreach, touchedAt < 90d │ SKIP — already being touched; don't interfere │

 └──────────────────────────────────────┴──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘

 Lookup runs BEFORE sequence-build, not after

 it affects sequence sizing + sending-cap math (5k/week per user — feedback_outreach_sending_cap_5k_weekly.md ).

 Promote as reusable tool

 Per the framework plan, this becomes tools/outreach_client.py::find_prospects_with_no_touch(emails, days=90) — a reusable bulk function, not a one-shot. Rule 18 compliance (never write a new one-shot when a

 reusable function will get called again). Returns the 3-bucket split.

 Plan-mode the 90-day filter tool (Phase 3 item from my earlier walkthrough) as the FIRST build, ahead of sequence copy. Once it returns real eligibility counts per sequence, we know actual cohort sizes and can

 size the send-per-week throttling.

 ❯ what does "(diff against S71 v2 base, extract shared voice)" mean?

 ⏺ Let me unpack both pieces.

 "Diff against S71 v2 base"

 At the end of Session 71 (yesterday), we built a Dormant Re-Engage v2 draft in a Google Doc ( 164JXmN0wZ7sz_d4_4SgPINJncsxumz5zwgzzhBLBLn0 ). You took that doc to claude.ai to dial in the copy further.

 "Diff" = compare your claude.ai-revised version side-by-side against the S71 v2 we started with. Find every change:

 - Subject line rewrites

 - Body paragraph changes

 - CTA phrasing shifts

 - Signature / link placement changes

 - Cadence/interval changes

 - Any tone or angle differences

 This tells us what YOU wanted different. Those changes are the direction.

 "Extract shared voice"

 The 14 sequences aren't 14 totally different emails — they share a foundation. The "shared voice" = the elements that STAY THE SAME across all 14:

 - Tone (conversational, no sales clichés, no em dashes)

 - Value prop emphasis (engagement → turn-key → esports → standards, per your priority order)

 - Step 1 word count rule (<80 words)

 - Step structure (5 steps, 5+ day cadence)

 - Signature format

 - Link placement ( codecombat.com/schools hyperlinked, meeting link in 1-2 steps)

 - CTA style ("would it be worth sending over info" not "hop on a call")

 - Breakup email structure

 These get captured as a shared base spec that every sequence inherits. Then each of the 14 sequences varies ONLY on the cohort-specific layer:

 - TC-Elem: "you created a free teacher account — your elementary students would love [specific thing]"

 - TC-HS: "you created a free teacher account — your high school students would love [specific thing, different from Elem]"

 - TC-Virtual: "you created a free teacher account — our curriculum works well for fully-online learning environments"

 - LIB: "you're a librarian/media specialist — here's how libraries are using CodeCombat as a coding resource"

 Same base voice. Different cohort angle. 14 variants built off one spec.

 Why this matters

 Without extracting the shared voice, we'd end up writing 14 totally independent sequences and they'd drift — Email 1 of TC-Elem would sound different from Email 1 of TC-HS in ways that have nothing to do with

 grade level. Same tone problems across 14 sequences means 14 sequences to iterate on separately.

 WITH a shared base, we iterate the base ONCE, then every sequence inherits the fix. That's why your revisions from claude.ai matter — whatever YOU changed should flow through to all 14.

 Does that make sense? And do you want to paste the revised copy now or grab it later?

 results, then paste your revised copy from claude.ai.

 ⏺ DRE Sequence Family — How We Got to 13

 Session 72, 2026-04-16 . Walkthrough of the reasoning, the data, and the decisions that collapsed yesterday's 21-sequence theoretical framework into today's 13-sequence data-backed family.

 ---

 Built a 21-sequence DRE framework organized as a substrategy × role × grade matrix :

 - TC (Teacher-Created free accounts): 9 variants = Dist-Admin + Sch-Admin × 3 grades + Teacher × 3 grades + IT + Curriculum

 - LQD (License/Quote/Demo requests): 9 variants (same matrix)

 - LIB (Library/Librarian): 2 variants

 - UNI (Universal Fallback, no role): 1 variant

 21 total. The problem: it was theoretical. We hadn't counted leads per bucket. We didn't know if the grade splits were justified or if we'd be building empty sequences.

 Today's work — let data reshape the plan

 Ran 5 classification passes on 76,471 measured SF Leads rows, then 2 filter passes.

 Pass 1 — baseline classification

 Full universe breakdown by role:

 admin 28,892 (measured — 37.78%)

 empty-title TC 24,491 (measured — 32.03%)

 IT 9,873 (measured — 12.91%)

 curriculum 4,252 (measured — 5.56%)

 teacher 3,416 (measured — 4.47%)

 empty-title other 2,513 (measured — 3.29%)

 other/unmatched 1,528 (measured — 2.00%)

 admin-support 1,106 (measured — 1.45%)

 library 379 (measured — 0.50%)

 Pass 2 — grade inference on the two biggest universals

 Attempted keyword-based grade detection from Company field on TC-Universal (25,167 measured) and INT-Universal (1,410 measured).

 TC-Universal split cleanly. Elem 3,657 / MS 4,809 / HS 4,342 / District 364 / Residual 11,593 — all measured. Three grade buckets well above any ship threshold.

 INT-Universal did NOT split cleanly. All grade cohorts came in under 100 measured. Forcing a grade split would create near-empty sequences.

 → First reframe: INT stays as a single Universal, not 9 variants. TC gets grade-split.

 Pass 3 — rule tweaks + new buckets surfaced from the data

 Four rule additions:

 - Standalone unified → District bucket (recovered 88 LAUSD-style measured rows)

 - Trailing ms abbreviation → MS bucket (recovered 335 measured rows)

 - Virtual/Cyber/Online academy → new TC-Virtual bucket (451 measured, concentrated in PA+OH cyber-charter states)

 - Homeschool → split into TC-Homeschool-Network (28 measured, borderline) and TC-Homeschool-Excluded (433 measured individual family accounts, dropped as non-customers)

 → Second reframe: Three buckets the original matrix didn't anticipate — TC-Virtual, TC-District, TC-All-Grades — emerged because the data structure had them.

 Pass 4 — NCES cross-reference (biggest single lift)

 Fuzzy-matched the 10,264 measured "residual" Company names against the Territory Schools tab (~60,000 measured schools) and lifted NCES Grade Span authoritative grade assignments. Recovered 2,542 measured rows

 from Residual into Elem/MS/HS buckets. Also surfaced 135 measured K-12 schools as TC-All-Grades (a new bucket).

 Pass 5 — state-aware disambiguation (final sweep)

 Ran state-filtering on the 1,699 measured "ambiguous" matches (common school names like "Lincoln Elementary" that exist in 5+ states). Recovered only 367 measured rows. Remaining residual is

 name-quality-limited — schools genuinely not in the NCES roster. Stopped enriching.

 Filter 1 — active account cross-check

 Cross-referenced every DRE lead's Company against the Active Accounts tab. Excluded leads where:

 - Fuzzy match to active account with Deal Level = district (CSMs handle)

 - Exact match to an active account at school level

 421 measured rows excluded. Bulk of exclusions were TC-MS and TC-HS, where active-customer overlap is highest.

 Filter 2 — 90-day Outreach no-touch

 Bulk-queried Outreach for every DRE email's touchedAt timestamp (478 measured API calls, 7 min wall). Bucketed into:

 - Not in Outreach (36 measured — these need prospect creation)

 - In Outreach, stale ≥90 days (25,991 measured — eligible for DRE)

 - In Outreach, touched <90 days (780 measured — skip, already being engaged)

 99.83% measured of eligible leads already exist in Outreach. Workflow is "add existing prospect to new sequence," not "create new prospect." Rule 17 (state + timezone) compliance is mostly verification, not

 population.

 1. GEN substrategy parked. When I proposed a "General Re-Engagement" substrategy for role-populated leads outside TC/LQD/LIB source whitelists, you caught that it belongs in cold outreach, not dormant

 re-engagement. ~48,000 measured rows (Zen Prospect/Agile/MCH/Gov Spend/K12Prospects) parked for a future cold-email session.

 2. UNI tightened to 22 interest-signal sources. Instead of routing any empty-title lead to UNI, you defined UNI as empty-title leads with a clear interest-signal Lead Source (conference, webinar, Hour of Code,

 Drift/Intercom chat, etc.). Prevents bought leads from getting dormant-re-engagement copy.

 3. Each substrategy gets its own Universal variant. TC-Universal for empty-title TC leads, LQD-Universal for empty-title LQD leads, INT-Universal for empty-title INT leads. One generic UNI would have mixed

 source contexts incorrectly.

 4. LIB collapsed 2 → 1. You flagged that 2 variants was overkill for 638 measured librarians.

 5. State-per-sequence not justified. Your Superintendent #7 sequences are state-split (13 variants) because admin messaging leans on state-specific legislative/budget context. DRE doesn't — {{state}}

 mergefield covers the personalization need. Confirmed option A (mergefield, not split).

 6. Code Ninjas excluded. 40 measured rows, you have a corporate deal.

 7. Homeschool individual families excluded. 433 measured rows, not customer-fit.

 8. TC-IT + INT-IT merged into IT-ReEngage. Each was below 200 measured alone; merged = 182 measured. IT messaging bridges both origin stories (Chromebook deployment, LMS integration).

 Final family (13 sequences, 26,137 measured eligible leads)

 Eligible % of DRE

 TC-Universal-Residual 6,957 26.6%

 TC-MS 5,452 20.9%

 TC-HS 4,892 18.7%

 TC-Elem 4,941 18.9%

 INT-Universal 867 3.3%

 LIB 633 2.4%

 TC-Virtual 441 1.7%

 TC-District 442 1.7%

 LQD-Universal 407 1.6%

 INT-Teacher 404 1.5%

 TC-Teacher 393 1.5%

 IT-ReEngage 182 0.7%

 TC-All-Grades 126 0.5%

 Key takeaways

 1. TC dominates the DRE universe — 89% measured of all eligible leads. The Teacher-Created free-account cohort is by far the biggest re-engagement target.

 2. The S71 matrix was over-engineered. Theoretical role × grade × substrategy splits produced dozens of near-empty buckets. Real data supports 13 variants, not 21 (and not the ~60 the fully-expanded matrix

 would have produced).

 3. NCES Grade Span enrichment was the single biggest lift. Pass 4 recovered 2,542 measured rows that keyword rules alone missed.

 4. 99.83% measured prospect existence in Outreach changes the add workflow. We're not creating prospects, we're adding existing prospects to new sequences.

 5. Cohort sizes drive the build order. INT-Universal ships first as safety net (867 measured, smallest viable universal). Then biggest TC cohorts. Then specialty variants (TC-Virtual, TC-District,

 TC-All-Grades). Then remaining tails (LIB, LQD, INT-Teacher, TC-Teacher, IT-ReEngage).

 ---

 exist in the NCES roster at all (7,006 measured had zero matches even in their own state).
